Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
6 min
Navigating the Book of Sales: Volume 8 Overview
Table of contents listing chapters and topics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main chapters and key rulings covered in Volume 8 of Ashraf al-Hidayah on the fiqh of sales.

Core Idea
The sale of fruit, options of stipulation and sight, and Hanafi rules for delivery and price certainty.

This lesson orients you to Volume 8 of Ashraf al-Hidayah, the Urdu commentary on Al-Hidayah. This volume focuses on the book of sales (kitab al-buyu'), especially the chapters on options (khiyarat). We will survey the major rulings listed in the table of contents to prepare for detailed study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main chapters
Scan the TOC to find the two chapter headings: باب خيار الشرط (Chapter of Option of Stipulation) and باب خيار الروية (Chapter of Option of Sight). These are the core sections of this volume.
Each chapter groups several rulings on that type of option.
2
Note key rulings on fruit sales and option duration
Look for rulings such as: the sale of fruit before and after ripening, the effect of stipulating ripening on trees, and the default three-day period for khiyar al-shart. Also note the issue of price payment timing.
These rulings illustrate the Hanafi insistence on certainty (gharar avoidance).
3
Recognize cross-madhhab differences
Observe that the TOC mentions a difference with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whether the option transfers to heirs upon the death of the option holder. The Hanafi position is that it does not transfer.
This is a key ikhtilaf that will be explored in detail in the chapter.

Table of contents of volume eight. The sale of fruit before and after ripening is permissible. Buying fruit and stipulating that it ripen on the trees makes the sale invalid. Ashraf al-Bidayah, Urdu commentary on Al-Hidayah, volume eight. If fruit is bought absolutely and then left on the trees with or without the seller's permission, ruling on increase. If fruit is bought absolutely and then the tree is rented for the fruit, ruling. If fruit is bought absolutely and then other fruit appears in it before or after possession, ruling on seeds. Ruling on measuring a specific amount of fruit. Ruling on the sale of wheat and rice in ears, and the sale of [?] and sesame in husk. Keys are included in the sale of a house. The wages of the weigher and the money-counter are on the seller. The wages of the one who weighs the price are on the buyer. In a sale in exchange for goods, the price should be handed over first, then the seller delivers the sold item. The duration of the option of stipulation, how many days? Statements of jurists. Chapter of option of stipulation. If something is bought on condition that the price is not paid for three days, the sale does not occur, but it is permissible in such a way? Ruling. Does the sold item leave the seller's ownership due to the seller's option? Will the sold item leave the seller's ownership due to the buyer's option? If the sold item is destroyed in the buyer's possession, it is destroyed in exchange for the price. If a wife is bought on a three-day option, the marriage is not invalid. First precedent of the mentioned issue. [page numbers] Second precedent. Third precedent. Fourth precedent. Fifth precedent. Sixth precedent. Seventh precedent. The one with the option can accept or reject the contract during the option period. Acceptance is valid in the absence of the other party, but rejection is not valid in this way. With the death of the one with the option, the option becomes invalid and does not transfer to heirs. Imam al-Shafi'i's view: The option of stipulation is established for both the buyer and others. Whichever of them enforces or rescinds the sale, the sale is executed or rescinded. If their statements occur together, one declaring the sale valid and the other declaring it void, which will be given effect? Two slaves were sold for a thousand dirhams on condition that there is a three-day option regarding one, the sale is invalid. If someone buys two garments on condition that he may take whichever he wants for ten dirhams and this option is for three days, the sale is valid; for three or four garments, such a sale is invalid. Ruling on combining option of specification with option of stipulation. If one item is destroyed or defective, its sale with its price is valid, and the other is an trust. If a house is bought with an option of stipulation and another house adjacent to it is sold and he takes it as pre-emption, this indicates consent to the purchase of the first house. Two persons buy a slave; both have an option. If one is pleased, can the other reject? Statements of jurists. If a slave is bought on condition that he is a baker or a scribe, and he turns out to be otherwise, the buyer may buy him for the full price or reject. [page numbers] Chapter of option of sight. The legal status of option of sight. Is there an option of sight in an item sold without being seen? Imam Abu Hanifa's view. Is there a specified time for option of sight? If one looks at the surface of a heap of wheat or a folded cloth, or sees the face of a slave girl, or the face and hind of a quadruped, there is no option. If one sees the courtyard of a house, the option of sight is terminated, even if he has not seen the rooms. Similarly, if one sees the house from outside or the garden from outside, there is no option of sight. The agent's seeing is the buyer's seeing. The method of option of sight for a blind person. If one of two garments is seen and both are bought, then the other is seen, seeing one is not sufficient for seeing the other.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents (فہرست) for the eighth volume of Ashraf al-Hidayah, an Urdu commentary on Al-Hidayah by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani. The volume covers the book of sales (kitab al-buyu'), particularly the chapters on options (khiyarat). The table lists the major topics and their corresponding page numbers in the original text. Key chapters include: option of stipulation (باب خيار الشرط) and option of sight (باب خيار الرؤية). Under each chapter, specific rulings are enumerated, such as the permissibility of selling fruit before and after ripening, the effect of stipulating ripening on trees, the inclusion of keys in a house sale, wage responsibilities for weighing and counting, and the rules regarding the death of the party holding the option. The table also notes differences with Imam al-Shafi'i on whether the option transfers to heirs. The numbering at the end of lines (e.g., 52, 53) indicates page references. This TOC serves as a roadmap for the student to navigate the detailed rulings on sale transactions in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
خیار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in a contract, typically for three days, during which the party with the option can confirm or rescind the sale.
خیار الرویة (khiyar al-ru'yat): The option for the buyer to cancel the sale if the purchased item was not seen before the contract, provided the buyer had no prior knowledge of it.
بیع (bay'): The contract of sale, involving transfer of ownership of an item (mabi') for a price (thaman).
ثمن (thaman): The price paid in a sale, which can be cash (naqd) or goods (saman).
مبیع (mabi'): The item being sold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The fruit belongs to the seller and the buyer has no claim.
B) The buyer owns the fruit and any increase.
C) The increase belongs to the seller.
D) The sale becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
Volume 8 of Ashraf al-Hidayah covers sales and options; knowing the TOC helps you quickly locate rulings on khiyar al-shart, khiyar al-ru'yat, and related disputes.

Ruling on Selling a Slave with a Condition to Free Him
Summary of ruling on conditional sale of slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a sale includes a condition not required by the contract and identify that the sale becomes fasid.

Core Idea
A condition not inherent to the contract makes the sale fasid.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of a sale depends on the contract being free from conditions that are not part of its essence. This lesson examines a specific case: selling a slave with a condition that the buyer will free him or grant him a status leading to freedom. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish between valid conditions and those that render a sale voidable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the added condition
Determine the subject matter (slave) and the condition imposed (buyer must free, make mudabbar, mukatib, or umm walad).
2
Classify the condition
Recognize that this condition is 'ghair muqtada al-aqd' – not required by the contract of sale itself. It is an extra benefit for the slave.
Conditions that are part of the contract's nature (e.g., warranty) are permissible.
3
State the ruling
The sale is fasid (voidable) because of this condition. The Hanafi school holds that such a condition invalidates the sale unless made permissible by istihsan.
Fasid differs from batil: fasid can be rectified by removing the condition, while batil cannot.
4
Apply the ruling to similar cases
Any sale with a condition that confers a benefit unrelated to the contract's core is similarly fasid.
For example, selling a car with the condition that the buyer donate it to charity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غلام اس شرط پر بیچا کہ مشتری آزاد کرے گا یامد بر بنائے گا یا مکاتب بنائے گا یا باندی کو ام ولد بنائے گا بیع فاسد ہے غیر مقتضی عقد شرط کا حکم
A slave is sold with the condition that the buyer will free him, or make him a mudabbar, or make him a mukatib, or make the slave-girl an umm walad – the sale is fasid (voidable). This is the ruling of a condition not required by the contract.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage summarizes a Hanafi ruling: selling a slave with a condition that the buyer performs an act that benefits the slave (like freeing him or granting him a status leading to freedom) renders the sale fasid. The condition is 'ghair muqtada al-'aqd' – not inherent to the contract. In Hanafi fiqh, such a condition invalidates the sale unless it is a recognized exception (e.g., by istihsan).

Key Terms
بیع فاسد (bay' fasid): A sale that is voidable due to a defect in subject matter or consideration, but can be rectified.
غیر مقتضی عقد (ghair muqtada al-aqd): Not inherent to the contract; a condition that is not required or implied by the contract itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on selling a slave with the condition that the buyer frees him?
A) The sale is valid and the condition is binding.
B) The sale is fasid (voidable).
C) The sale is batil (void).
D) The sale is makruh.

Key Takeaway
A condition not required by the contract renders the sale fasid in Hanafi fiqh.

Sale of Cloth with Condition of Tailoring
Ruling on selling cloth with condition of tailoring

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a sale with an extra service condition and distinguish between fasid and batil.

Core Idea
A sale is fasid if it includes a condition requiring the seller to perform an additional service not integral to the exchange.

In Hanafi fiqh, certain conditions added to a sale can render it invalid. This passage gives a specific example: buying cloth on condition that the seller also tailors it into a garment. We will examine why this makes the sale fasid and what that means in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the added condition
The act is a sale of cloth. The condition is that the seller must cut the cloth into a shirt or cloak.
2
Classify the condition
Determine if the condition is part of the exchange (muqtada al-aqd) or an extra service (ghair muqtada). Here, tailoring is not integral to the sale of cloth.
3
Apply the rule of extra conditions
Any condition that imposes an obligation on either party beyond the exchange itself makes the sale fasid (voidable).
4
Understand the consequence
The sale is fasid, meaning it is not automatically void but can be rectified by removing the condition or fulfilling it voluntarily after the contract.
5
Note the remedy
If the condition is dropped or the tailoring is done without being part of the contract, the sale becomes valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کپڑا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ بائع اسے کاٹ کر کرتا یا قباءہی دے تو بیع فاسد ہے
Cloth is bought with the condition that the seller cuts it into a shirt or qaba (cloak) – the sale is fasid.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This is another example of a condition ghair muqtada al-'aqd: the seller is required to perform an additional service (tailoring) beyond the sale of the cloth itself. Hanafi fiqh deems such a sale fasid because the condition imposes an extra obligation not inherent to the exchange of goods for price.

Key Terms
بیع فاسد (bay' fasid): A voidable sale that can be rectified if the condition is removed or fulfilled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if cloth is sold with the condition that the seller cuts it into a shirt?
A) Valid by istihsan.
B) Fasid (voidable).
C) Batil (void).
D) Makruh.

Key Takeaway
A sale with a condition requiring the seller to perform an extra service not integral to the exchange is fasid in Hanafi law.

Sale of Shoes with Condition of Repair – Exception by Istihsan
Ruling on sale with repair condition by istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits a sale with a repair condition, state the role of istihsan, and distinguish when a condition renders a sale fasid versus permissible by custom.

Core Idea
Istihsan permits a sale with a repair condition because custom (urf) overrides strict qiyas.

In Hanafi fiqh, a sale contract normally requires that the price and item be known and free from conditions not part of the contract. However, a well-established custom can create an exception. This lesson examines a specific ruling: selling shoes with the condition that the seller will adjust them or provide straps. Though such a condition would normally invalidate the sale by qiyas, the Hanafi school permits it by istihsan—juristic preference based on widespread custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
The act is a sale of shoes. The condition is that the seller will adjust the shoes or make straps. This is not a standard part of a shoe sale.
Normally, a sale must be unconditional except for conditions that are required by the contract itself, like payment terms.
2
State the general qiyas ruling
By strict analogy (qiyas), any condition that is not demanded by the contract (ghair muqtada al-'aqd) makes the sale fasid (defective) because it introduces uncertainty (gharar) or an additional obligation.
Qiyas here would nullify the sale.
3
Recognize the exception by istihsan
The Hanafi school departs from qiyas due to istihsan: juristic preference based on custom and necessity. The sale is permissible.
Istihsan is a source of law in the Hanafi madhhab, allowing for equity.
4
Understand the basis: custom ('urf)
It is customary in the marketplace for shoemakers to adjust and repair shoes as part of the sale. This widespread, continuous custom makes the condition acceptable.
Custom is recognized as a source when there is no contrary text.
5
Contrast with other schools
The Shafi'i school, which does not accept istihsan, would rule such a condition invalid and the sale fasid. They rely solely on qiyas.
This highlights the practical difference (thamarah) between schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جوتا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ بائع اسے برابر کر دے گا یا تسمہ بنا کر دے گا تو بیع استحسانا جائز ہے
Shoes are bought with the condition that the seller will adjust them or make straps – the sale is permissible by istihsan.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This ruling is an exception to the general principle that conditions ghair muqtada al-'aqd invalidate the sale. By istihsan (juristic preference), the Hanafi school permits such a sale because it is customary in the market for shoemakers to provide adjustments. This is based on the principle that custom ('urf) can override qiyas when it is widespread and not contrary to a clear text.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that allows departure from qiyas for a stronger reason, such as custom or necessity.
عرف (urf): Custom or prevalent practice that can influence legal rulings when not contradicting a clear text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling on selling shoes with a repair condition, why is the sale permissible?
A) It is based on a clear text from the Quran.
B) It is based on analogical reasoning (qiyas) to other sales.
C) It is based on istihsan (juristic preference) due to custom.
D) It is based on necessity (darurah).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a sale with a customary condition of repair is valid by istihsan, overriding the default qiyas rule.

Possession in Fasid Sale: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Difference between Hanafi and Shafi'i on fasid sale possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ownership transfer in a fasid sale and explain the Shafi'i counterargument, identifying the practical difference between the two schools.

Core Idea
In a fasid sale, possession with permission transfers ownership in Hanafi; not in Shafi'i.

This passage presents a key point of divergence between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: does the buyer become owner of the purchased item in a voidable (fasid) sale simply by taking delivery with the seller's consent? The answer determines whether the buyer can use or dispose of the item before the defect is resolved. Understanding this dispute clarifies how each school conceptualizes the link between possession and ownership.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds the buyer becomes owner of the sold item in a fasid sale when possession is taken with the seller's permission, provided both counter-values are property (not wine, pork, etc.).
The Hanafi view relies on a hadith: 'Whoever takes possession with permission becomes owner.'
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees: ownership does not transfer in a fasid sale until the sale is made valid or the goods are returned.
Shafi'i does not distinguish fasid from batil; any defect in contract prevents ownership transfer.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i reasoning: a fasid sale is not a valid contract of exchange, so it cannot transfer ownership. Mere possession without a valid title is insufficient.
Shafi'i emphasizes the contract's validity at the moment of transfer.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand that Hanafis argue possession with permission is analogous to a valid sale (qiyas) because the seller's consent substitutes for the missing element, and ownership is established pending resolution (return or payment).
The Hanafi view separates the contract's defect from the possessory effect.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: Shafi'i requires immediate return of the goods without ownership; Hanafi allows the buyer to own them pending payment or return, affecting liability for loss and right to use.
Hanafi: buyer bears risk of loss and can use the item; Shafi'i: seller retains risk until contract is perfected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مشتری نے بیع فاسد میں مبیع پر بائع کے امر سے قبضہ کیا اور عقد میں دونوں عوض مال ہیں مشتری بیع کا مالک بن جائے گا اور قیمت لازم ہوگی ، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
In a fasid sale, if the buyer takes possession with the seller's permission, and both counter-values are property, the buyer becomes owner of the sold item and the price becomes obligatory – view of Imam Shafi'i.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage presents a point of view attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the effect of possession in a fasid sale. The Hanafi school also holds that possession with permission transfers ownership of the subject matter, but the buyer must either return the item or pay its value (or the agreed price if it is known). The mention of 'both counter-values are property' means that the sale involved lawful goods (not wine or pork). The dispute likely revolves around whether ownership transfers immediately or only after the price is paid. The text notes this as Shafi'i's view, implying a comparison.

Key Terms
بیع فاسد (bay' fasid): A sale voidable by nature but which may become valid upon removal of the defect.
قبضہ (qabd): Taking physical possession or delivery of the sold item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented, what happens to the buyer in a fasid sale after taking possession with the seller's permission?
A) The buyer must return the item immediately.
B) The buyer becomes owner but owes the price.
C) The sale becomes valid automatically.
D) The buyer cannot own the item at all.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, possession with permission in a fasid sale transfers ownership to the buyer, who must pay the price—unlike the Shafi'i view where ownership remains with the seller until the contract is perfected.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Rulings on Profit from Mistaken Payment and Disliked Sales
Index of rulings on profit and disliked sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on profit from a mistaken payment and identify which sales are disliked (makruh) in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Profit from a mistakenly paid debt is halal; najsh and selling during Friday adhan are makruh tahrimi.

This lesson draws from the table of contents of Volume 8 of Ashraf al-Hidayah, which outlines key rulings in the Book of Sales. The first entry addresses a scenario where a plaintiff receives payment but later both parties agree no debt was owed—the profit from using that money is permissible. The subsequent section lists several disliked sales, including najsh (deceptive bidding), meeting caravans (talaqqi), selling at the time of Friday adhan, and separating mahram slaves without consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling on mistaken payment
Read the opening line: the plaintiff claimed money, the defendant paid, then both truthfully said no debt existed. Determine the hukm on the profit derived from that money.
The text states 'the profit is halal'—this is a clear ruling.
2
Distinguish between types of disliked sales
From the fihrist, list the sales mentioned under 'فصل فيما يكره': najsh, talaqqi, sale at Friday adhan, bay' man yazid, and separation of slaves. Note that each has a specific hukm (karahah).
The fihrist gives brief statements; the full Hidayah will provide conditions and proofs.
3
Apply the Hanafi understanding of karahah
Recognize that 'makruh' in the Hanafi school can be either tahrimi (prohibited) or tanzihi (disliked). From context, selling at Friday adhan is makruh tahrimi, as it implies neglect of an obligation.
Najsh is considered haram by many Hanafis; the fihrist mentions 'definition and legal status' without explicit hukm level.
4
Note the exception for adult mahram slaves
The fihrist states that separating two adult slaves who are mahram is not makruh, whereas separating minor mahram slaves is. Understand the basis: for adults, there is no harm in separation as they can consent.
This shows the nuanced application of karahah based on circumstances.

The plaintiff claimed money from the defendant; the defendant paid the money; then both truthfully said that the defendant owed no money, yet the plaintiff benefited from those dirhams, so the profit is permissible. Section on what is disliked. The legal status and definition of najsh. Talaqqi jalb when the people of the city are harmed; but the ruling is: for a villager, the city-dweller selling on his behalf. Sale at the time of the Friday adhan is disliked. The reason for dislike in the mentioned sales. Ruling on bay' man yazid. Ruling on separating two minor slaves when they are mahram relatives. Separating is disliked. Separating two adult slaves who are mahram relatives is not disliked. Legal status of iqalah. Ruling on the condition of decrease or increase from the first price. The condition of increase over the first price is void. Ruling on iqalah with other than the genus of the first price. Chapter of iqalah. Destruction of the price does not affect the validity of iqalah, but destruction of the sold item prevents iqalah. Iqalah on the remaining part is valid after destruction of one part. Chapter of murabahah and tawliyah. Definition of murabahah and tawliyah, legal status of both sales; it is necessary that the capital be known. The wages of the launderer, engraver, dyer, rope-maker, and seed-sower are included in the capital. What words should the seller use? If the buyer becomes aware of fraud in murabahah, does he have the right to enforce or rescind the sale? Opinions of jurists. Ruling on a buyer who bought cloth then sold it at profit and then bought it. A slave authorized to trade bought cloth for ten dirhams and owes so much debt that it covers his net worth; he sold to the master for fifteen dirhams; at what price can the master sell it as murabahah? A mudarib bought cloth for ten dirhams and sold to the owner of capital for fifteen; at what price can the owner sell it as murabahah? A slave-girl was bought and became one-eyed, or she became a widow and grew old; at what price can he sell as murabahah? If he or a stranger poked out her eye and the buyer received compensation from him, at what price can he sell the slave-girl as murabahah? He bought cloth; a rat tore it or fire burned it; at what price can he sell as murabahah? He bought a slave on credit for one thousand, sold for one hundred profit without stating; can the buyer return it or not? The first buyer bought a slave on credit for one thousand rupees, sold for eleven hundred. The second buyer killed the slave, then learned of the credit; the second buyer is liable for eleven hundred. If the first buyer sold to the second by tawliyah without stating, what is the ruling on return? The buyer appointed someone as his representative. In a sale of tawliyah, if the buyer does not know at what price it was acquired, the sale is void. It is not permissible to sell movable or transferred property without possession. Is sale of real estate before possession permissible? Opinions of jurists. He bought a measurable or weighable item with the condition of measurement or weighing, then measured or weighed and took possession, then the buyer sold with the condition of measurement or weighing; for the second buyer, the ruling on selling and eating before measurement or weighing. Disposal of the price before possession is permissible. The buyer's increase in the price, the seller's increase in the sold item, and the ruling on the seller decreasing the price. He sold with ready price then deferred for a known period; the transaction becomes deferred. If the creditor gives respite to the debtor, the debt becomes deferred. Chapter of riba. Selling a measurable or weighable item with its own genus with disparity is riba; the effective cause of riba. The effective cause of riba according to Hanafis and Shafi'is. The evidence of the Hanafis. Selling a measurable or weighable item equally is permissible. One handful for two handfuls; one apple for two apples; the sale is not permissible.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents (fihrist) for the eighth volume of Ashraf al-Hidayah, an Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani. The volume covers several important chapters from the Book of Sales (Kitab al-Buyu'), including sections on disliked sales (fimā yukrah), bay' al-najsh (auction fraud), talaqqi al-jalab (meeting caravans), sale at the time of Friday adhan, bay' min yazid (sale by increase), separation of slaves, iqalah (rescission), murabahah (cost-plus sale), tawliyah (resale at cost), and riba (usury). The index lists specific rulings and points of fiqh that will be elaborated in the text. For instance, under iqalah, it notes that destruction of the price does not affect iqalah, but destruction of the sold item prevents it. Under murabahah, it highlights the need for the capital to be known and discusses various scenarios of fraud, defects, and calculation of profit. The section on riba covers the Hanafi position on the effective cause (illah) of riba (measurement and weight) in contrast to the Shafi'i position (food and currency). The fihrist serves as an organizational tool, allowing students to locate specific discussions. The commentary in the volume will expand on each topic with proofs and differences of opinion.

Key Terms
نجش (najsh): In the fihrist, it is listed as a chapter on its definition and legal status; it refers to bidding up the price without intending to buy.
تلقی جلب (talaqqi al-jalab): Meeting caravans outside the city to buy goods before they reach the market, often causing harm to locals.

Key Takeaway
Profit from a mistakenly paid debt is halal, and several sales are makruh in the Hanafi school, including najsh, talaqqi, and selling during Friday adhan.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Why Kitab al-Buyu Follows Kitab al-Waqf: Placement and Linguistic Foundations
Explains placement and linguistic analysis of 'bay''

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Book of Sale follows the Book of Endowment in Al-Hidayah and identify the linguistic features of the word bay' as a word of opposite meanings.

Core Idea
Waqf and sale both remove ownership, so Al-Hidayah places them together.

The author of Al-Hidayah arranged topics from pure worship to mixed worship-transactions to pure transactions. Understanding the sequence requires recognizing the shared attribute between waqf and sale—both extinguish ownership. This lesson also examines the linguistic features of bay' and its related terms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's sequence of topics
In the commentary, first pure worship (prayer, fasting, zakat, hajj), then something combining worship and transaction (marriage), then pure transactions (sale, pre-emption).
2
Note the shared attribute between waqf and sale
Both remove ownership from the owner: waqf removes endowed property from the endower, sale removes sold item from the seller. This is the 'muzil al-milk' connection.
3
Examine the linguistic issue with the plural 'buyu''
Bay' is a masdar, which normally has no plural. Two answers: either it is used as ism maf'ul (sold items) hence plural, or it is masdar but plural due to diverse types of sale.
4
Recognize bay' as addad (word with opposite meanings)
Bay' can mean both selling and buying. The commentary cites two hadiths: one where it means sell, another where it means buy.
5
Confirm that shira'/ishtira' are also addad
These words also mean both selling and buying, as seen in Quran 2:90 where ishtira' means sell.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم .
كتاب البيوع
ترجمہ یہ کتاب بیع کے احکام کے بیان میں ہے
تشریح صاحب کتاب نے سب سے پہلے خالص عبادات نماز ، روزہ ، زکوۃ، حج کو بیان کیا پھر ایسی چیز کو بیان فرمایا جو سن وجہ عبادت ہے اور من وجہ معاملہ ہے۔ یعنی نکاح اور اس کے متعلقات ۔ اب یہاں سے ان چیزوں کو بیان کریں گے جو خالص معاملات کے قبیل سے ہیں۔ یعنی بیع اور شفعہ وغیرہ ۔ فاضل مصنف نے کتاب البیوع کو کتاب الوقف کے بعد ذکر کیا ہے۔ ان دونوں کے درمیان مناسبت یہ ہے کہ دونوں میں سے ہر ایک مالک کی ملک کو زائل کر دیتا ہے۔ چنانچہ وقف شئی موقوفہ کو واقف کی ملک سے خارج کر دیتا ہے۔ اور بیع شئی مبیع کو بائع کی ملک سے خارج کر دیتی ہے۔ بہر حال ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک مزیل ملک ہے۔ پس اس مناسبت کی وجہ سے کتاب الوقف کے بعد کتاب البیوع کو ذکر فرمایا۔
لفظ بیع کی تحقیق بیوع بیع کی جمع ہے یہاں یہ سوال ہو گا کہ لفظ بیع مصدر ہے اور مصدر کا تثنیہ اور جمع نہیں آتا۔ پس یہاں بیوع بصیغہ جمع ذکر کیا ہے۔ اس کا ایک جواب تو یہ ہے کہ بیع بیع اسم مفعول کے معنی میں ہے اور مبیعات کی بہت سی انواع اور اقسام ہیں۔ اس لئے اس کو جمع کے صیغہ کے ساتھ ذکر کیا گیا۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ بلا شبہ مصدر ہے لیکن انواع بیع کے مختلف ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کو جمع کے صیغہ کے ساتھ ذکر فرمایا ہے۔ لفظ بیع اضداد میں سے ہے۔ یعنی لغت میں بیج کا لفظ اخراج الشئ عن الملک بمال اور ادخال الشئ في الملک بمال پر بولا جاتا ہے۔ یعنی مال کے عوض کسی چیز کو ملک سے نکالنے پر بھی بولا جاتا ہے۔ اور مال کے عوض کسی چیز کو ملک میں داخل کرنے پر بھی بولا جاتا ہے۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ لفظ بیع کے معنی بیچنے کے بھی آتے ہیں اور خریدنے کے معنی بھی آتے ہیں۔ حدیث اذا خلف النوعان فبيعو اكکیف شئتم میں معنی اول ( بیچنا ) ہی مراد ہیں اور حدیث بیع احد کم علی بیع احیہ میں معنی ثانی ( خرید نا ) مراد ہیں یعنی تم میں سے کوئی آدمی اپنے بھائی کے خریدنے کی صورت میں نہ خریدے۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر مسلمان کوئی چیز خریدنے کے ارادہ سے بھاؤ میں نہ کہ
کرتا ہے تو تم اس کو خریدنے کے ارادہ سے درمیان میں مت گھو۔ دیکھئے یہاں بیچ بمعنی شراء استعمال کیا گیا ہے۔
اس طرح لفظ شراء اور اشتراء اضداد میں سے ہے۔ یعنی یہ لفظ بھی بیچنے اور خریدنے کے معنی میں مشترک ہے۔ مثلاً
بتسما اشتروا به انفسهم
میں لفظ اشتراء بیچنے کے معنی میں مستعمل ہے یعنی بڑی ہے وہ جس کے بدلے بیچا انھوں نے اپنے آپ کو ۔ (البقر ۹۰:۲۰)

میں بھی اسی معنی میں استعمال کیا گیا ہے۔ یعنی اور بہت ہی بری چیز ہے جس کے بد ۱۰۱ انھوا
besturdubooks.wordpress.com
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The Book of Sales. Translation: This book is about the rulings of sale. Commentary: The author first mentioned pure acts of worship: prayer, fasting, zakat, and Hajj. Then he mentioned something that is an act of worship in one respect and a transaction in another, namely marriage and its related matters. Now from here he will mention things that are pure transactions, i.e., sale, pre-emption, etc. The distinguished author mentioned the Book of Sale after the Book of Waqf. The appropriateness between the two is that both remove ownership from the owner. Thus, waqf removes the endowed property from the ownership of the endower, and sale removes the sold item from the ownership of the seller. In any case, both are removers of ownership. So due to this connection, he mentioned the Book of Sale after the Book of Waqf. Investigation of the word bay': Buyu' is the plural of bay'. Here a question arises: the word bay' is a masdar (verbal noun), and the masdar does not have a dual or plural. So why has buyu' been mentioned in the plural form? One answer is that bay' is used in the sense of ism maf'ul (the passive participle, meaning that which is sold), and there are many types and kinds of sold items. Therefore it is mentioned in the plural form. The second answer is that undoubtedly it is a masdar, but due to the different types of sale, it has been mentioned in the plural form. The word bay' is one of the addad (words with opposite meanings). That is, in the language, the word bay' is used for removing a thing from ownership in exchange for wealth, and also for bringing a thing into ownership in exchange for wealth. So it is applied to the removal of something from ownership in exchange for wealth, and also to the entry of something into ownership in exchange for wealth. The conclusion is that the word bay' carries the meanings of both selling and buying. In the hadith 'When the two types differ, then sell as you wish', the first meaning (selling) is intended. And in the hadith 'Let none of you buy over the purchase of his brother', the second meaning (buying) is intended, meaning no one among you should buy in the situation where his brother is buying. The meaning is that if a Muslim is negotiating to buy something, do not intervene with the intention to buy. See here, 'bay'' has been used in the sense of 'shira'' (buying). Similarly, the words 'shira'' and 'ishtira'' are among the addad. That is, these words are shared between selling and buying. For example, (Quran 2:90) 'They have sold themselves for a bad price' – here 'ishtara' is used in the sense of selling, i.e., evil is that for which they sold themselves. And (Quran 2:90) 'Evil is what they have sold themselves for' – this too is used in the same sense, i.e., evil is the thing for which they sold themselves.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the Book of Sales. The commentator first explains the author's arrangement of topics: after pure worship (prayer, fasting, zakat, hajj), he discussed marriage (which combines worship and transaction), and now moves to pure transactions, starting with sale. He justifies placing the Book of Sale after the Book of Endowment by noting that both remove ownership: waqf removes the endowed property from the endower's ownership, and sale removes the sold item from the seller's ownership. Then he addresses a linguistic point: the title 'Kitab al-Buyu' uses the plural form 'buyu'' of 'bay''. Since 'bay'' is a verbal noun (masdar), which normally does not have a plural, two explanations are given: either 'bay'' is used as a passive participle (meaning 'sold items') which come in many types, or the plural is used due to the diversity of sale types. He then explains that the word 'bay'' is one of the 'addad' (words with opposite meanings) in Arabic, meaning it can mean both selling and buying. He supports this with two hadiths: one where 'bay'' means selling, and another where it means buying. He also notes that 'shira'' and 'ishtira'' can likewise mean both selling and buying, citing Quranic verses where 'ishtira'' means 'sell'. This linguistic analysis is foundational for understanding the terminology used throughout the Book of Sales in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
بیع (bay'): A verbal noun (masdar) that lexically means both selling (exchange of property for compensation) and buying. In fiqh, it is used for the contract of sale.
شراء / اشتراء (shirā' / ishtirā'): Also from the 'addad' category; lexically means both buying and selling. In the Quranic verse cited (2:90), it means selling (i.e., bartering away one's soul for a small price).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author of Al-Hidayah place Kitab al-Buyu after Kitab al-Waqf according to this commentary?
A) Because both involve transfer of ownership
B) Because both are acts of worship
C) Because both require witnesses
D) Because both are invalid without a contract

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi arrangement of fiqh topics is not arbitrary; it follows a logical progression from pure worship to transactions, and the linguistic analysis of key terms like bay' reveals the depth of legal methodology.

Linguistic Meaning of Bay' in the Quran
Linguistic parsing of bay' in the Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Quranic verses where bay' and its derivatives mean selling or buying, and explain how this linguistic range supports the Hanafi legal definition of bay' as an exchange.

Core Idea
Bay' in the Quran can mean both buying and selling — a lexical flexibility underpinning the Hanafi contract definition.

This passage surveys multiple Quranic verses to demonstrate that the Arabic root b-y-' and its cognates (shira', ishtira) are used for both selling and buying. The author begins with the story of Yusuf (sold for a low price) and then moves to verses where individuals 'sell' their souls or 'purchase' misguidance. Understanding this semantic range is crucial because the Hanafi school defines a sale contract (bay') as a mutual exchange of property, and this linguistic foundation justifies that technical definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first verse and its verb
Find the verse about Yusuf: 'و شروه بثمن بخس' (12:20). Note that the verb 'sharaw' means 'they sold' here, not 'bought'.
The verb is from the same root as bay'.
2
Examine the second verse
Read the verse 'ومن الناس من يشرى نفسه ابتغاء مرضات الله' (2:207). Here 'yashri' also means 'sells' (his soul). Confirm that the same root can indicate selling.
The context determines the meaning.
3
Analyze verses with shira'/ishtara
Go through the remaining verses (4:44, 3:199, etc.). Note that in each, the words 'shatara'/'ishtara' clearly mean 'buy' or 'purchase', often metaphorically.
Pay attention to the object: 'purchase misguidance', 'purchase with a small price'.
4
Summarize the semantic range
Conclude that bay' and its derivatives can denote both selling and buying in Quranic Arabic. The specific meaning is determined by context and grammatical structure.
This flexibility is key for the Hanafi legal definition.
5
Connect to Hanafi fiqh
Understand that the Hanafi definition of bay' as 'exchange of property for property' embraces both sides of the transaction. The Quranic usage provides a lexical basis for this inclusive definition.
The term bay' in fiqh refers to the contract as a whole, not just one party's action.

Book of Sales. This is the meaning in the verse: 'And they sold him for a low price' (12:20) — meaning they sold him, their brother, for a deficient price. Commentary
This passage is a linguistic exploration of the word bay' (and its synonyms shira' and ishtira) as used in the Quran. The author begins by referencing the story of Yusuf (AS) where the verb 'sharaw' (و شروه) is used for selling. Then he notes that the same verb 'yashri' (یشرى) in 2:207 means selling one's soul. He then demonstrates that the words shira' and ishtira are used in many verses to mean buying or purchasing, often in a metaphorical sense (e.g., exchanging guidance for misguidance). The purpose is to show the semantic range of bay' in Arabic: it can mean both buying and selling, and occurs in multiple contexts. This sets the stage for the technical definition of bay' as a legal term. The commentary follows the author's order: first the verse about selling Yusuf, then the verse about selling oneself, then several verses where shira' and ishtira mean buying. The author does not provide a specific ruling here; rather, he is establishing the lexical foundation.

Key Terms
بيع (bay'): In this passage, bay' and its derivatives (shira', ishtira) are shown to have both selling and buying meanings in Quranic usage.
شراء / اشترى (shira' / ishtara): Used in the Quran to mean buying or purchasing, often metaphorically.

The Hanafi Definition of Bay' (Sale)
Defines bay' terminologically with three qualifiers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi technical definition of bay' and identify which contracts are excluded by each qualifier.

Core Idea
Bay' is an exchange of property for property, with mutual consent, by way of trade—each qualifier excludes a specific type of contract.

The Hanafi school defines bay' with precision to distinguish it from other contracts like lease, marriage, or conditional gifts. This lesson unpacks the three qualifiers of the definition and shows how each one carves out a distinct legal category.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three parts of the definition
Break down the phrase 'mubadala al-mal bil-mal bi al-taradi bi tariq al-tijara' into its three constituent qualifiers: exchange of property, mutual consent, and by way of trade.
Each qualifier serves to exclude a different contract type.
2
Analyze the first qualifier: exchange of property
Consider which contracts involve an exchange but not of property for property. Ijarah exchanges property for benefits; nikah exchanges property for the right to intimacy. Both are excluded because property is not exchanged for property.
Mal must be valuable, owned, and permissible in Islamic law.
3
Analyze the second qualifier: mutual consent
Examine why a coerced sale (bay' al-mukrah) is invalid. The verse 4:29 requires trade by mutual consent, so any transaction without free will falls outside valid bay'.
Hanafis consider silence as consent if there is evidence of satisfaction.
4
Analyze the third qualifier: by way of trade
Contrast bay' with hibah bi shart al-'iwad (gift with compensation). Both involve exchange of property, but only the former is done with the intention of trade (tijara). The definition restricts bay' to commercial transactions.
Custom and intention determine whether an exchange is trade.
5
Understand the term 'tamlik' in the definition
The author clarifies that 'exchange' in the definition means 'tamlik'—transferring ownership. Bay' is an ownership transfer of property for property, not just possession or use.
This distinguishes bay' from other transfers like lending or gifting.

بیع کی اصطلاحی تعریف اریک کی معطلی تین بیع مبادلة المال بالمال بالتراضى بطريق التجارة کو کہتے ہیں یعنی باہمی رضا مندی سے تجارت کے طریقہ پر مال کو مال کے بدلے میں لینا۔ مبادلتہ المال بالمال کی قید سے اجارہ اور نکاح خارج ہو گئے ۔ کیونکہ اجارہ میں مبادلہ المال بالمنافع ہوتا ہے۔ اور نکاح میں مبادلة المال بالبضع ہوتا ہے۔ اور بالتراضی کی قید سے مکرہ کی بیع خارج ہوگئی کیونکہ مقصود بیع نافذ کو بیان کرنا ہے اور مبادلہ بلاتر اپنی بیع شرعی نہیں ہوتا۔ چنانچہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے یا ایها الذین آمنوالاتا كلوا أموالكم بينكم بالباطل الا ان تكون تجارة عن تراض منكم - بطريق التجارة کی قید سے ہبہ بشرط العوض خارج ہو گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ ہبہ بشرط العوض میں بھی مبادلة المال بالمال ہوتا ہے مگر بطریق التجارة نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ یہ خیال رہے کہ تعریف میں مبادلہ سے مراد تملیک ہے۔ یعنی مال کے بدلے میں مال کا مالک کر دینا۔ بیع کا مشروع ہونا قرآن، حدیث اور اجماع تینوں سے ثابت ہے۔ قرآن سے مثلايا ايها الذين آمنوالاتا كلوا أموالكم بينكم بالباطل الا ان تكون تجارة عن تراض منکم ۔اے ایمان والو! نہ کھاؤ مال ایک دوسرے کے آپس میں ناحق مگر یہ کہ تجارت ہو آپس کی خوشی سے۔ اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ باہمی رضامندی سے بیع شراء جائز اور مشروع ہے۔ دوسری آیت

حديث نمبر ..... عن قيس بن ابى غرزة قال كنا في عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نسميَّ السَّما سرة فمرَّ بنا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قسما ناباسم هوا حسن منه فقال يا معشر التجار ان البيع يحضره اللغو و الحلف فشو بوه بالصدقة - قیس بن ابی غریزہ سے روایت ہے کہ ہمارا یعنی گروہ تجار کا رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانے میں سماسرہ نام تھا۔ پھر رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ہمارے پاس تشریف لائے اور ہمارا نام پہلے نام سے بہتر رکھا اور آپ نے فرمایا اے معشر تجار یعنی سوداگروں کے گروہ بیچ میں لغوا اور قسم دونوں موجود ہوتے ہیں۔ اس لئے تم اپنی بیجوں کو صدقہ سے ملا دو ۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ بیج اور شراء کے مقدمات میں اکثر لغو اور بے فائدہ قسم وغیرہ کا اتفاق پڑتا ہے۔ تو اس کے کفارہ کے لئے کچھ لالہ صدقہ دیا کرو (ابوداؤد کتاب البیوع ) اور ترندی جلد اصفحہ ۲۲۹ میں ہے یا معشر التجار ان الشيطان والاثم يحضر ان البيع فشو بو ابيعكم

حدیث نمبر ... عن ابي سعيد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال التاجر الصدوق الامين مع النبين والصديقين ۲ والشهداء - ابوسعید خدری فرماتے ہیں کہ رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ سچا اور امانت دار تاجر (قیامت کے روز ) نبیوں، صدیقوں اور شہیدوں کے ساتھ ہو گا۔ (ترمذی ج اص ۲۲۹)
The terminological definition of bay': it is called 'mubadala al-mal bil-mal bi al-taradi bi tariq al-tijara' — meaning exchanging property for property by mutual consent in the manner of trade. By the restriction 'exchanging property for property', ijara (lease) and nikah (marriage) are excluded because in ijara the exchange is of property for benefits (manafi'), and in nikah the exchange is of property for the right of intercourse (bud'). By the restriction 'by mutual consent', the sale of a coerced person (mukrah) is excluded because the intention is to describe a valid sale (bay' nafidh), and an exchange without consent is not a valid Islamic sale. As Allah says: 'O you who believe, do not consume your wealth among yourselves unjustly, except that it be trade with mutual consent' (4:29). By the restriction 'by way of trade', hibah bi shart al-'iwad (gift with a condition of compensation) is excluded because in hibah bi shart al-'iwad there is also an exchange of property for property, but it is not by way of trade. It should be noted that in the definition, 'exchange' refers to tamlik (making someone owner) — i.e., making someone the owner of property in exchange for property. The legitimacy of bay' is established by the Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma. From the Quran: first, the verse 4:29 — 'O you who believe, do not consume your wealth unjustly, except it be trade with mutual consent.' This shows that buying and selling with mutual consent are permissible and prescribed. A second verse: 'Allah has permitted sale and forbidden usury' (2:275). This verse also indicates the permissibility of sale. Hadith 1: From Qays ibn Abi Gharazah: 'We used to be called simsara (brokers) in the time of Allah's Messenger (SAW). Then the Prophet (SAW) passed by us and called us by a name better than that (i.e., traders) and said: O assembly of traders, indeed sale is attended by idle talk and oaths, so mix it with charity.' (Abu Dawud, Kitab al-Buyu') and in Tirmidhi (vol. 1, p. 229) it is: 'O assembly of traders, indeed Shaytan and sin attend sale, so mix your sale with charity.' Hadith 2: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: The Prophet (SAW) said: 'The truthful, trustworthy trader will be with the prophets, the truthful (siddiqin), and the martyrs (on the Day of Judgment).' (Tirmidhi, vol. 1, p. 229)
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage provides the technical definition of bay' (sale) as a legal contract and establishes its legitimacy. The definition is: 'mubadala al-mal bil-mal bi al-taradi bi tariq al-tijara' — an exchange of property for property with mutual consent by way of trade. The author explains each part: 'exchange of property' excludes ijarah (lease, which exchanges property for benefits) and nikah (marriage, which exchanges property for the right to intimacy). 'Mutual consent' excludes coerced sales, as invalid. 'By way of trade' excludes conditional gifts (hibah bi shart al-'iwad), which involve exchange but not as trade. The definition uses 'tamlik' (making owner) for mubadala. Then the author proves the legitimacy of bay' from three sources: Quran (verse 4:29 and 2:275), Sunnah (two Hadith about traders and charity), and Ijma (consensus, implied). The first Hadith acknowledges that sales involve idle talk and oaths, so charity is recommended to purify. The second Hadith encourages truthfulness and trustworthiness. This lesson is foundational for Kitab al-Buyu', establishing the basic definition and legal basis of sales.

Key Terms
مبادلة المال بالمال (mubadala al-mal bil-mal): The exchange of property for property, which excludes contracts like ijarah (exchange for benefits) and nikah (exchange for sexual rights).
بالتراضى (bi al-taradi): With mutual consent, excluding coerced transactions which are invalid in Islamic law.
بطريق التجارة (bi tariq al-tijara): By way of trade, which excludes gifts with compensation (hibah bi shart al-'iwad) that are not considered commercial transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ijarah (lease)
B) Nikah (marriage)
C) Hibah bi shart al-'iwad (gift with compensation)
D) Sale of a coerced person

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of bay' is a precise legal tool that uses three qualifiers to isolate true commercial sales from other property exchanges.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Proofs of Legitimacy of Bay' from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma
Establishes legitimacy of bay' using Quran, Hadith, and Ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to cite the Quranic verses and Hadith that establish the permissibility of bay' and explain how each proof indicates its legitimacy.

Core Idea
Bay' is legitimized by the Quran (2:275 'Ahalla Allah al-bay''), the Sunnah (Hadith advising charity in sales), and Ijma.

Having defined bay' technically, the author now proves that sale is a legitimate contract. Three sources are cited: the Quranic verse that explicitly permits sale, Hadith that recognize the practice and encourage charity to purify it, and the consensus of scholars (Ijma). This lesson examines each proof and its legal import.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sources of legitimacy
The text states that bay' is established by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma. Locate each source in the passage.
Ijma is mentioned but not elaborated; it is implied by the author.
2
Analyze the first Quranic proof (4:29)
Read the verse 'illa an takuna tijaratan 'an taradin minkum'. How does it indicate permissibility? The exception 'illa' implies that trade by mutual consent is allowed. This is a primary proof for the permissibility of sale.
Hanafis use the principle 'al-istithna' yufidu al-ibahah' (exception indicates permissibility).
3
Analyze the second Quranic proof (2:275)
The verse 'ahalla Allah al-bay' wa harrama al-riba' explicitly declares sale halal. The word 'ahalla' is a clear declaration of permissibility (ibahah).
This is a qat'i al-thubut (definitive transmission) but zanni al-dalala (probable meaning) because 'ahalla' could imply permissibility or obligation; context shows it is permissibility.
4
Examine the Hadith proofs
Two Hadith are cited: one from Qays ibn Abi Gharazah where the Prophet called traders by a better name and said sale is attended by idle talk and oaths, so mix it with charity. The second from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri promises reward for truthful traders. Both indirectly recognize the validity of sale by offering guidance on it.
The Hadith do not directly say 'sale is halal' but assume its permissibility by addressing its conduct.
5
Understand the role of Ijma
The author mentions Ijma as the third source. The consensus of the Ummah across generations that sale is permissible. This is a secondary proof reinforcing the textual evidence.
Ijma is based on the continuous practice of Muslims since the time of the Prophet.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner

The Definition of Bay' (Sale) in Hanafi Fiqh
Definition of bay' with exclusions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of bay' and identify which contracts are excluded by each component of the definition.

Core Idea
Bay' is not every exchange of property—it must be mutual, commercial, and involve property for property.

In Hanafi fiqh, a precise definition of sale (bay') is essential to distinguish it from other transactions such as hire, marriage, coerced sales, and conditional gifts. This lesson breaks down the classical definition into its constituent parts and explains how each part excludes a different type of contract. Understanding this definition is the foundation for all rules of buying and selling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the complete definition
Read the full Arabic definition: 'مبادلة المال بالمال بالتراضی بطريق التجارة'. Translate each term: exchange (mubaadalah), property for property (al-mal bi al-mal), with mutual consent (bi al-tarāḍī), by way of trade (bi ṭarīq al-tijārah).
Memorize the definition as it is the basis for all sale contracts.
2
Analyze the first exclusion: 'property for property'
Understand that 'exchange of property for property' excludes ijarah (hire) where property is exchanged for benefits (manafi'), and nikah (marriage) where property (mahr) is exchanged for sexual enjoyment (bud'').
Both ijarah and nikah involve property on one side only, not both.
3
Analyze the second exclusion: 'with mutual consent'
This excludes any sale under duress (al-bay' al-mukrah). The Quranic proof (4:29) is cited to show that valid trade requires mutual consent.
Coerced sales are invalid (ghayr nāfidh) in Hanafi law.
4
Analyze the third exclusion: 'by way of trade'
This excludes hibah bi shart al-'iwad (gift with compensation) because although it involves exchange of property, it is not done in a commercial manner.
The difference lies in intention and practice: trade implies profit motive and customary commercial form.
5
Clarify the meaning of 'exchange' as 'tamlik'
The author notes that 'exchange' here means transfer of ownership (tamlik), i.e., making someone the owner of property in return for other property. This distinguishes bay' from other transfers like permissible gifts.
Tamlik is a key concept: sale transfers full ownership, not just possession or use.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بیع کی اصطلاحی تعریف یعنی مبادلة المال بالمال بالتراضی بطريق التجارة کو کہتے ہیں یعنی باہمی رضا مندی سے تجارت کے طریقہ پر مال کو مال کے بدلے میں لینا۔ مبادلتہ المال بالمال کی قید سے اجارہ اور نکاح خارج ہو گئے ۔ کیونکہ اجارہ میں مبادلہ المال بالمنافع ہوتا ہے۔ اور نکاح میں مبادلة المال بالبضع ہوتا ہے۔ اور بالتراضی کی قید سے مکرہ کی بیع خارج ہوگئی کیونکہ مقصود بیع نافذ کو بیان کرنا ہے اور مبادلہ بلاتر اپنی بیع شرعی نہیں ہوتا۔ چنانچہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے یا ایها الذین آمنوالاتا كلوا أموالكم بينكم بالباطل الا ان تكون تجارة عن تراض منكم - بطريق التجارة کی قید سے ہبہ بشرط العوض خارج ہو گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ ہبہ بشرط العوض میں بھی مبادلة المال بالمال ہوتا ہے مگر بطریق التجارة نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ یہ خیال رہے کہ تعریف میں مبادلہ سے مراد تملیک ہے۔ یعنی مال کے بدلے میں مال کا مالک کر دینا۔
The terminological definition of sale: it is called 'exchange of property for property with mutual consent by way of trade,' meaning taking property in exchange for property on the method of trade with mutual consent. The restriction 'exchange of property for property' excludes hire (ijarah) and marriage (nikah), because in hire there is an exchange of property for benefits, and in marriage there is an exchange of property for sexual enjoyment. The restriction 'with mutual consent' excludes a coerced sale, because the intent is to mention an effective sale, and exchange without consent is not a legitimate sale. Thus Allah Most High says: 'O you who believe, do not consume your property among yourselves wrongfully, unless it be a trade with mutual consent.' The restriction 'by way of trade' excludes a gift with a condition of compensation (hibah bi shart al-'iwad), because in a gift with compensation there is also an exchange of property for property, but not by way of trade. It should be noted that by 'exchange' in the definition is meant 'transfer of ownership,' i.e., making one owner of property in exchange for property.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the legal term bay' (sale) as used in the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating the technical definition: 'the exchange of property for property with mutual consent by way of trade.' Each part of this definition excludes other contracts. First, 'exchange of property for property' excludes ijarah (hire), where property is exchanged for benefits (manafi'), and nikah (marriage), where property (mahr) is exchanged for the right to sexual enjoyment (budd'). Second, 'with mutual consent' excludes a sale under duress (mukrah), as such a sale is not valid (ghayr nafidh) because it lacks consent. The author cites the Quranic verse (4:29) which permits trade based on mutual consent. Third, 'by way of trade' excludes a gift with a condition for compensation (hibah bi shart al-'iwad), because although it involves an exchange of property, it is not conducted in the manner of commerce. Finally, the author clarifies that 'exchange' in the definition means transfer of ownership (tamlik), i.e., making someone the owner of property in return for other property.

Key Terms
بیع (bay'): Exchange of property for property with mutual consent by way of trade.
مبادلة المال بالمال (mubaadalah al-mal bi al-mal): Exchange of property for property, excluding contracts where one side is not property (such as benefits or sexual right).
تراضی (tarāḍī): Mutual consent, which excludes coerced contracts.
بطريق التجارة (bi ṭarīq al-tijārah): By way of trade/commerce, excluding gifts and other non-commercial exchanges.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which contract is excluded from the definition of bay' by the phrase 'by way of trade' (بطريق التجارة)?
A) Ijarah (hire)
B) Nikah (marriage)
C) Hibah bi shart al-'iwad (gift with compensation)
D) Sale under duress

Key Takeaway
A valid sale in Hanafi fiqh requires four elements: property-for-property exchange, mutual consent, trade-like conduct, and transfer of ownership.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
8 min
The Legitimacy of Sale: Proof from Quran, Hadith, and Ijma
Proving the permissibility of sale using scriptural and consensus sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sources proving the permissibility of sale and explain the Hanafi interpretation of the key Quranic verse (4:29) and the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Sale is permitted by the Quran, confirmed by the Prophet, and agreed upon by the Ummah — but requires honesty and charity.

This passage establishes that sale (bay') is a legitimate activity in Islam, backed by the primary sources of Shari'ah: the Quran, the Sunnah, and the consensus (ijma) of the Muslim community. The author presents these proofs in a layered manner, starting with explicit Quranic verses, then prophetic hadiths that both encourage honest trade and warn against its pitfalls, and finally pointing to the continuous practice of the Prophet and the Companions. Understanding these proofs is essential for recognizing that trade is not only permissible but can be a form of worship when conducted with integrity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sources
Recognize that the passage proves permissibility from Quran, Hadith, and Ijma. This is the standard hierarchy of Islamic legal proofs.
Hanafi usul gives priority to Quran and mutawatir sunnah, then ahad hadith, then ijma.
2
Analyze the Quranic evidence
Examine verse 4:29: 'لا تأكلوا أموالكم بينكم بالباطل إلا أن تكون تجارة عن تراض منكم'. The exception clause ('except it be trade with mutual consent') positively permits sale. Also note verse 2:275 which contrasts halal sale with haram riba.
The phrase 'عن تراض' emphasizes mutual consent as a condition for valid sale.
3
Analyze the Hadith evidence
Three hadiths are cited: (1) Prophet advising merchants to mix sales with charity due to idle speech and oaths; (2) promise of high rank for truthful merchant; (3) warning that most merchants are wicked except those who fear Allah and are truthful. All affirm the permissibility while adding moral guidance.
The hadiths serve both as proof and as ethical instruction.
4
Understand the Ijma evidence
The passage states that from the time of the Prophet to today, Muslims have unanimously agreed on the permissibility of sale. It provides examples of the Prophet trading and major Companions engaging in various trades.
Ijma is a binding proof; the Hanafis accept the consensus of the Companions as authoritative.
5
Note the moral dimension
The proofs do not merely permit sale; they encourage honesty, charity, and God-consciousness. The passage ends with a discussion of the best earnings, showing that trade is ranked highly after jihad.
This reflects the Hanafi view that earning halal income is a form of worship.

قیس بن ابی غریزہ سے روایت ہے کہ ہمارا یعنی گروہ تجار کا رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانے میں سماسرہ نام تھا۔ پھر رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ہمارے پاس تشریف لائے اور ہمارا نام پہلے نام سے بہتر رکھا اور آپ نے فرمایا اے معشر تجار یعنی سوداگروں کے گروہ بیچ میں لغوا اور قسم دونوں موجود ہوتے ہیں۔ اس لئے تم اپنی بیجوں کو صدقہ سے ملا دو ۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ بیج اور شراء کے مقدمات میں اکثر لغو اور بے فائدہ قسم وغیرہ کا اتفاق پڑتا ہے۔ تو اس کے کفارہ کے لئے کچھ لالہ صدقہ دیا کرو (ابوداؤد کتاب البیوع ) اور ترندی جلد اصفحہ ۲۲۹ میں ہے یا معشر التجار ان الشيطان والاثم يحضر ان البيع فشو بو ابيعكم بالصدقة . حدیث نمبر ... عن ابي سعيد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال التاجر الصدوق الامين مع النبين والصديقين ۲ والشهداء - ابوسعید خدری فرماتے ہیں کہ رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ سچا اور امانت دار تاجر (قیامت کے روز ) نبیوں، صدیقوں اور شہیدوں کے ساتھ ہو گا۔ (ترمذی ج اص ۲۲۹) حدیث نمبر ... عن اسماعيل بن عبيد بن رفاعه عن ابيه عن جده انه خرج مع النبي الى المصلى فراى الناس يتبايعون فقال يا معشر التجار فاستجابو الرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ورفعو اعناقهم وابصار هم اليه فقال ان التجار يبعثون يوم القيامة فجاراً الامن اتقى الله وبر وصدق ۔ حضرت رفاعہ سے روایت ہے کہ میں ایک مرتبہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے ہمراہ عید گاہ کی طرف نکلا تو آپ نے دیکھا کہ لوگ خرید فروخت کر رہے ہیں۔ آپ نے فرمایا اے تاجروں کے گروہ یہ سب رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی طرف متوجہ ہو کر آپ کی بات سننے لگے اور اپنی گرد نہیں اور آنکھیں آپ کی طرف اٹھا ئیں آپ نے فرمایا کہ تا جر قیامت کے دن فاجر نا فرمان گنہ گار اٹھائے جائیں گے ۔ مگر وہ جو اللہ سے ڈرا اور نیکی کی اور بیچ بولتا رہا۔ ( ترندی جاش ۱۲۳۰) ان بد ایات ثلاثہ میں سے پہلی روایت میں تاجروں کو صدقہ کرنے کی ہدایت کی گئی ہے۔ اور دوسری اور تیسری روایت میں بچے اور دیانت دار تاجر کی منقبت اور ستائش کی گئی ہے۔ تینوں روایات تجارت اور بیع کے جواز پر دلالت کرتی ہیں۔ اجماع بھی جواز بیع پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ کیونکہ عہد رسالت سے لے کر آج تک تمام مسلمان جو از بیچ پر متفق چلے آرہے ہیں۔ چنانچہ ارباب سیر نے تحریر کیا ہے کہ نبوت سے پندرہ سال پہلے آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ام المومنین خدیجہ الکبری کے واسطے تجارت فرمائی ہے۔ اور ا کا بر صحابہ مثلاً صدیق اکبر فاروق اعظم ، عثمان غنی ، عباس ، عبدالرحمن بن عوف رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہم نے تجارت کی ہے ۔ چنانچہ حضرت ابو بکر کپڑے کے تاجر تھے اور حضرت عمر فلہ کے تاجر تھے ۔ حضرت عثمان کپڑے اور کھجور کی تجارت کرتے تھے۔ اور حضرت عباس عطر فروش تھے ۔ عبدالرحمن بن عوف لکھی اور پنیر کی تجارت کرتے تھے۔ ملاعلی قاری نے شرح نقایہ میں لکھا ہے کہ علماء احناف نے فرمایا کہ جہاد کے بعد سب سے بہتر کمائی تجارت ہے پھر زراعت ہے پھر صنعت و حرفت ہے۔ ملاعلی قاری کہتے ہیں کہ میرے نزدیک افضل کسب کتابت (خوش نویسی) ہے۔
The legislation of sale is established by the Quran, Hadith, and Ijma (consensus). From the Quran: 'O you who believe, do not consume your property among yourselves wrongfully, unless it be a trade with mutual consent' [4:29]. This verse shows that buying and selling with mutual consent is permissible and legislated. The second verse: 'Allah has permitted sale and forbidden usury' [2:275]. This verse also indicates the permissibility of sale. Hadith: From Qays ibn Abi Gharazah: 'We used to be called brokers in the time of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Then the Prophet passed by us and gave us a better name, saying: O company of merchants, indeed sale is attended by idle speech and oaths, so mix it with charity.' (Abu Dawud, Kitab al-Buyu'). Hadith: From Abu Sa'id from the Prophet: 'The truthful, honest merchant will be with the prophets, the truthful, and the martyrs' (Tirmidhi). Hadith: From Isma'il ibn Ubayd ibn Rifa'ah from his father from his grandfather: 'He went out with the Prophet to the prayer place and saw people trading. He said: O company of merchants! They responded and raised their necks and eyes to him. He said: The merchants will be raised on the Day of Resurrection as wicked, except those who fear Allah, do good, and are truthful.' (Tirmidhi). These three narrations indicate the permissibility of trade and sale. Ijma also indicates the permissibility of sale, because from the time of the Messenger to today, all Muslims have agreed on the permissibility of sale. Thus the biographers have written that fifteen years before prophethood, the Prophet traded on behalf of Khadijah al-Kubra. And the major Companions such as Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, Umar al-Faruq, Uthman Ghani, Abbas, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf (may Allah be pleased with them) engaged in trade. Abu Bakr was a cloth merchant, Umar a palm merchant, Uthman traded in cloth and dates, Abbas was a perfume seller, and Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf traded in butter and cheese. Mulla Ali Qari wrote in Sharh al-Nuqayah that the Hanafi scholars said: The best earning after jihad is trade, then agriculture, then craftsmanship. Mulla Ali Qari said: In my view, the best earning is calligraphy (kitabat).
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a proof section establishing the legal permissibility (mashru'iyyah) of sale (bay'). The author cites three sources: The Quran, the Sunnah (three hadiths), and Ijma (consensus). The primary Quranic proof is verse 4:29, which permits trade based on mutual consent. A second verse (2:275) explicitly permits sale while forbidding usury. Three hadiths are then quoted: The first is from Qays ibn Abi Gharazah, where the Prophet advised merchants to mix their sales with charity due to the presence of idle speech and oaths in transactions. The second is from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, promising the truthful and trustworthy merchant a high rank with prophets, the truthful, and martyrs. The third is from Rifa'ah, warning that most merchants will be raised as wicked except those who fear Allah and are truthful. These hadiths, while containing warnings, nevertheless confirm the permissibility of trade. Finally, the author cites Ijma (consensus) of the ummah from the time of the Prophet to the present, noting that the Prophet himself traded and major Companions engaged in various trades. The passage ends with a discussion by Mulla Ali Qari about the best earnings: trade is best after jihad (according to Hanafi scholars), though Mulla Ali Qari personally holds calligraphy as superior. This entire passage serves to prove that sale is a legitimate and encouraged form of earning.

Key Terms
مشروع (mashrū‘): Legislated or sanctioned by the Shari'ah; permissible/proven from divine sources.
اجماع (ijmā‘): Consensus of the mujtahid scholars of the ummah on a ruling.
تاجر صدوق امین (tājir ṣadūq amīn): A truthful and trustworthy merchant, who is promised a high rank in the Hereafter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Perform a special prayer
B) Mix it with charity
C) Avoid all oaths
D) Seek forgiveness after each sale

Key Takeaway
Sale is legitimate in Islam based on clear Quranic permission, prophetic guidance, and the continuous consensus of the community, with an emphasis on honesty and charity.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner

The Wisdom, Conditions, and Pillar of Sale
States wisdom, hukm, conditions, and pillar of sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the wisdom behind the legislation of sale, identify the two conditions for its validity, and recognize the pillar of sale according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Sale was legislated for lawful exchange of necessities; its effect is ownership, requiring sanity of parties and valuable deliverable property, with offer and acceptance as its pillar.

This lesson introduces the foundational elements of a sale (bay') in Hanafi fiqh. The text begins by explaining the divine wisdom (hikmah) for permitting trade: human interdependence necessitates lawful exchange to avoid haram means. It then states the legal effect (hukm) of a valid sale — transfer of ownership (milk) — and lists the two essential conditions (shurut) for validity: the contracting party must be sane, and the subject matter must be valuable property capable of delivery. Finally, it identifies the single pillar (rukn) of sale: offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul). Understanding these components is crucial for distinguishing a valid sale from a defective or void one.

Guided Path
1
Understand the wisdom (hikmah)
Read the opening sentences that explain why sale was legislated. Note the principle of human interdependence: no one produces all necessities; lawful exchange is needed to avoid haram means.
The wisdom is not a condition or pillar but the rationale behind the ruling.
2
Identify the hukm (legal effect)
The text states the hukm of sale is 'milk' (ownership). This means the buyer acquires full ownership and the right to valid disposal (tasarruf sahih).
Ownership is the consequence of a valid sale, not a condition.
3
Extract the conditions (shurut)
Two conditions are explicitly listed: (1) the contracting party ('aaqid) must be sane ('aaqil), and (2) the subject matter (mabe') must be valuable property (maal mutaqawwim) and capable of delivery (maqdoor al-tasleem).
Conditions are prerequisites; if missing, the sale is either void or defective.
4
Recognize the pillar (rukn)
The pillar of sale is offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul). Without these, no contract exists.
The pillar is the essence of the contract; its absence makes the contract non-existent.
5
Distinguish between shurut and rukn
Shurut are external requirements that must exist for validity, while the rukn is the internal essential component. Missing a condition may render the sale fasid (defective) but missing the rukn makes it batil (void).
This distinction is fundamental in Hanafi contract law.

Source Text

بیع مشروع ہونے کا سب تعلق البقاء المعلوم اللہ تعالی علی وجہ تمہیں ۔ یعنی زندگی جو خدا کو معلوم ہے اس کو اچھے طریقہ پر باقی رکھنا۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بقائے زندگی کے لئے جن چیزوں کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے وہ سب کسی ایک آدمی کے گھر تیار نہیں ہوتیں بلکہ ایک سامان کوئی تیار کرتا ہے ۔ اور دوسرا سامان کوئی تیار کرتا ہے ۔ پس ضروریات زندگی پورا کرنے کے لئے ہر شخص دوسرے کا محتاج ہوگا ۔ اب دوسرے آدمی سے اپنی ضروریات کی چیزوں کو حاصل کرنا حرام طریقہ پر ہو گا یا حلال طریقہ پر ہوگا ۔ حرام طریقہ سے حاصل کرنا تو شرعاً ممنوع ہے۔ اس لئے بیع کے حلال طریقہ کو مشروع کیا گیا ہے۔ بیع کا حکم ملک ہے۔ یعنی مشتری کو تصرف صبیح پر قدرت دینا۔ جواز بیع کی شرطیں، (1) عاقد کا عاقل ہونا (2) مبیع کا مال متقوم اور مقدور التسلیم ہونا۔ بیج کا رکن ایجاب اور قبول ہے۔
The reason for the legislation of sale is the preservation of life known to Allah Almighty in a good manner. That is, to preserve life, which is known to Allah, in a good manner. Its meaning is that all the things needed for the preservation of life are not prepared in one person's home; rather, one prepares one item and another prepares another item. Therefore, to fulfill the necessities of life, every person will be in need of another. Now, obtaining one's necessary items from another person could be by a haram method or by a halal method. Obtaining by a haram method is prohibited by Shari'ah. Therefore, the halal method of sale was legislated. The ruling (hukm) of sale is ownership (milk), i.e., giving the buyer the power of valid disposal. Conditions for the validity of sale: (1) The contracting party must be sane ('aaqil). (2) The subject matter must be valuable property (maal mutaqawwim) and capable of delivery (maqdoor al-tasleem). The pillar (rukn) of sale is offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul).
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage states the wisdom (hikmah) behind the legislation of sale, followed by its conditions and pillar. The wisdom is based on human interdependence: no single person can produce all necessities of life, so lawful exchange through sale is legislated to avoid unlawful means. The author then states the ruling (hukm) of sale: it is transfer of ownership (milk), giving the buyer the power of valid disposal (tasarruf sahih) over the purchased item. Two conditions (shart) for validity are explicitly mentioned: (1) the contracting party must be sane (not a minor insane person), and (2) the subject matter must be valuable property (maal mutaqawwim) and capable of delivery (maqdoor al-tasleem). The pillar (rukn) of sale is offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul). Note: In Hanafi fiqh, conditions and pillars are distinct; conditions are prerequisites for validity, while the pillar is an essential component of the contract. The passage does not mention all conditions (e.g., neither party being in a state of Ihram, etc.) but highlights these two as fundamentals.

Key Terms
ملک (milk): Ownership; the legal effect of a valid sale is that the buyer becomes owner of the subject matter.
مال متقوم (māl mutaqawwim): Property that is legally valuable and permissible to use in Shari'ah.
مقدور التسلیم (maqdūr al-taslīm): Capable of delivery; the subject matter must be physically and legally deliverable at the time of contract.
ایجاب و قبول (ījāb wa qabūl): Offer and acceptance; the two utterances that constitute the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the pillar (rukn) of a sale according to this passage?
A) The sanity of the parties
B) The subject matter being valuable
C) Offer and acceptance
D) Exchange of property

Key Takeaway
The validity of a sale in Hanafi fiqh depends on the sanity of the parties, the subject matter being valuable and deliverable, and the presence of offer and acceptance.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
