قال والاعواض المشار اليها لا يحتاج الى معرفة مقدارها فى جواز البيع لان بالاشارة كفاية في التعريف وجهالة الوصف فيه لا تُفضى الى المنازعة والاثمان المطلقة لا تصح الا ان تكون معروفة القدر والصفة لان التسليم والتسلم واجب بالعقد وهذه الجهالة مفضية الى المنازعة فيمتنع التسليم والتسلم وكل جهالة هذه صفتها تمنع الجواز هذا هو الأصل ترجمه قدوری نے کہا اور وہ بعوض جن کی طرف اشارہ کر دیا گیا۔ بیع جائز ہونے کے واسطے ان کی مقدار جاننے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ شناخت کے واسطے اشارہ کافی ہوتا ہے اور اس میں وصف کا مجہول ہونا جھگڑے کا سبب نہیں ہوتا اور جو شمن مطلق ہیں (ان سے) عقد صحیح نہیں ہو گا مگر یہ کہ مقدار اور صفت معلوم ہو کیونکہ سپر د کرنا اور قبضہ لینا بحکم عقد واجب ہے۔ اور چونکہ یہ جہالت جھگڑے کا سبب ہو گی اس لئے دینا اور لینا ممتنع ہوگا اور ہر ایسی جہالت جس کی یہ صفت ہو وہ بیع جائز ہونے سے مانع ہے۔ یہی اصل ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے بیع کے عوض خواہ شمن ہو یا مبیع ہو جب اس کی طرف اشارہ کر دیا گیا تو جواز بیع کے لئے اس کی مقدار جاننے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً یہ کہا کہ میں نے گندم کی یہ ڈھیری ان درہم کے عوض خریدی جو میرے ہاتھ میں ہیں تو یہ بیع جائز ہے۔ حالانکہ نہ مبیع یعنی گندم کی مقدار معلوم ہے اور نہ درہم کی مقدار معلوم ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ شناخت کے واسطے اشارہ کافی ہے ۔ اور وصف کا مجہول ہونا یعنی مشار الیہ کی مقدار کا معلوم نہ ہونا ایسا امر نہیں ہے جو جھگڑا پیدا کرے حالانکہ مانع جواز ایسی جہالت ہوتی ہے جو عاقدین کے درمیان جھگڑا پیدا کرے پس جب ایسی جہالت نہیں پائی گئی تو بیع بھی درست اور جائز ہوگی۔ واضح ہو کہ عوض اگر اموال ربویہ میں سے ہوں مثلاً درہم ، دنا نیر ، گندم اور جو، اور ان کو انکی جنس کے عوض فروخت کیا جائے اور ان کی مقدار معلوم نہ ہو تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے اگر چہ ان کی طرف اشارہ کیا گیا ہو۔ مثلاً درہم کو درہم کے عوض یا گندم کو گندم کے عوض بیچا اور دونوں کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے تو یہ بیچ نا جائز ہے اگر چہ
He said: And the counter-values that are pointed to do not require knowing their quantity for the validity of the sale, because pointing is sufficient for identification, and ignorance of the description therein does not lead to dispute. As for absolute prices, the sale is not valid unless they are known in quantity and description, because delivery and taking possession are obligatory by the contract, and this ignorance leads to dispute, thus delivery and taking possession become impossible. And every ignorance having this quality prevents validity. This is the principle. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And the counter-values that are pointed to do not require knowing their quantity for the validity of the sale, because pointing is sufficient for identification, and ignorance of the description therein does not lead to dispute. As for absolute prices, the contract is not valid unless their quantity and description are known, because delivery and taking possession are obligatory by the contract, and since this ignorance causes dispute, giving and taking become impossible. And every ignorance having this quality prevents the validity of the sale. This is the principle. Explanation: The issue is that when the counter-value in a sale, whether it be the price or the sold item, is pointed to, then for the validity of the sale, knowing its quantity is not necessary. For example, if one says: I bought this heap of wheat in exchange for these dirhams that are in my hand, then this sale is valid, even though neither the quantity of the wheat (the sold item) nor the quantity of the dirhams is known. The evidence is that pointing is sufficient for identification, and ignorance of the description, i.e., not knowing the quantity of the pointed item, is not something that creates dispute. Since the impediment to validity is the ignorance that creates dispute between the parties, when such ignorance is not found, the sale will be valid. It is clear that if the counter-values are from ribawi items, for example dirhams, dinars, wheat, and barley, and they are sold in exchange for their own genus and their quantity is not known, then it is not permissible even if they are pointed to. For example, selling dirhams in exchange for dirhams, or wheat in exchange for wheat, when the quantity of both is not known, then such a sale is impermissible, even if...
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the specification of counter-values in a sale. The principle is that identification of the subject matter is sufficient for validity if the item is present and pointed to, even if its exact quantity is unknown, because such ignorance does not lead to dispute. However, for absolute prices (such as unspecified money or fungible goods), ignorance of quantity and description renders the sale invalid because it prevents proper delivery and leads to dispute. The text gives the example of selling a heap of wheat for a handful of dirhams where both are pointed to: the sale is valid despite unknown quantity, because presence eliminates dispute. But if the goods are ribawi (like wheat for wheat), the sale is invalid if both quantities are unknown, even if pointed to. The exception for ribawi goods is because in such exchanges, equality of quantity is a condition.

Key Terms
عوض مشار الیہ (ivadh mushar ilayh): A counter-value (price or sold item) that is pointed to at the time of contract, making identification by sight sufficient even if quantity is unknown.
ثمن مطلق (thaman mutlaq): An absolute price, i.e., a price that is not specified in quantity or description, e.g., 'some dirhams' without stating how many.
جہالت مفضیہ الی المنازعہ (jahl mufdi ila al-munaza'ah): Ignorance that leads to dispute; such ignorance prevents the validity of the sale because it hinders peaceful delivery and fulfillment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sale where the buyer says 'I buy this heap of wheat for these dirhams in my hand,' and both are pointed to but the quantity of each is unknown, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The sale is invalid because quantity is unknown
B) The sale is valid because pointing suffices for identification
C) The sale is valid only if the wheat is weighed after the contract
D) The sale is invalid because it involves a ribawi item

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates sales of pointed goods despite unknown quantity, but requires exact specification for absolute prices; the key is whether ignorance leads to dispute.

Hanafi Refutation of Khiyar al-Majlis Proof
Completes Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i's proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi argument against khiyar al-majlis and evaluate why the hadith 'al-bayyi'ani bi'l-khiyar' is interpreted as khiyar al-qabul.

Core Idea
The hadith's 'khiyar' refers to khiyar al-qabul, not physical separation—a difference in interpreting the present tense.

This passage completes the Hanafi refutation of Imam al-Shafi'i's proof for khiyar al-majlis (option of the session). The core dispute lies in the interpretation of the word 'mutabay'i'an' in the hadith. The Hanafi commentator provides two arguments: a linguistic analysis showing that the word's real meaning (present tense) points to khiyar al-qabul, and a broader reasoning that even if ambiguous, the interpretation that avoids harming others' rights is chosen.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested hadith
The hadith 'al-bayyi'ani bi'l-khiyar ma lam yatafarraqa' is used by Shafi'i to prove khiyar al-majlis. Note the key terms: bayyi'ani (the two parties) and khiyar (option).
The dispute is over the word 'mutabay'i'an' and its tense implication.
2
Analyze the Hanafi linguistic argument
The Hanafi argues that 'mutabay'i'an' is an ism fa'il (active participle), which in its real meaning indicates the present state (between offer and acceptance). The present state refers to the time after offer but before final acceptance, where only khiyar al-qabul can apply.
This is a usul al-fiqh principle: haqiqah vs. majaz.
3
Examine the second Hanafi argument (harm prevention)
Even if ambiguity exists, taking 'khiyar' as khiyar al-majlis would harm the other party's right (by allowing revocation after mutual agreement). Therefore, khiyar al-qabul is preferred to avoid injustice.
This uses the qa'ida: al-darar yuzal (harm must be removed).
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Shafi'i, a buyer can cancel the sale during the session before physical separation. Under Hanafi, the sale is binding once both parties verbally agree.
Practical consequence: a buyer cannot change their mind after saying 'I bought' if the seller already said 'I sold'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سے ان کو متبابعان کہا گیا اور اسی صورت میں یہ حقیقت ہے کیونکہ یہ بات اپنی جگہ مسلم ہے کہ اسم فاعل حال کے معنی میں حقیقت ہے اور ماضی اور مستقبل کے معنی میں مجاز ہے۔ پس چونکہ اول کے دو معنی مجازی ہیں۔ اور تیسرا معنی حقیقی ہے اور حقیقت پر محمول کرنا اولیٰ ہے بہ نسبت مجاز پر محمول کرنے کے اس لئے حدیث میں متبایجان کے تیسرے معنی مراد ہوں گے اور تیسرے معنی مراد لینے کی صورت میں یعنی ایجاب کے بعد اور قبول آخر سے پہلے خیار قبول ہی مراد ہو سکتا ہے نہ کہ خیار مجلس پس ثابت ہوا کہ حدیث میں خیار سے مراد خیار قبول ہے اور خیار قبول مراد ہونے کی صورت میں مذکورہ حدیث امام شافعی کا مستدل نہ ہو سکے گی۔ او یحتملہ سے دوسرا جواب ہے۔ اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں اگر خیار سے حتماً خیار قبول مراد نہیں ہے۔ لیکن احتمال خیار قبول کا بھی ہے۔ یعنی بالخیار میں خیار سے خیار قبول بھی مراد ہو سکتا ہے۔ اور خیار مجلس مراد ہو سکتا ہے۔ مگر چونکہ خیار مجلس مراد لینا ابطال حق غیر کا سبب ہے اس لئے خیار قبول پر محمول کیا جائے گا نہ کہ خیار مجلس پر اور تفرق سے مراد تفرق اقوال ہے یعنی خیار قبول ثابت ہے جب تک کہ عاقدین قولاً متفرق نہ ہو جائیں اور اگر دونوں قولاً متفرق ہو گئے ۔ بایں طور کہ ان میں سے ایک نے بعث اور دوسرے نے اشتریت کہا تو اس کے بعد خیار باقی نہ رہے گا۔
They were called mutabay'i'an, and in this form it is the real meaning, because it is accepted in its place that ism fa'il is real in the meaning of the present tense and metaphorical in the meaning of past and future. So since the first two meanings are metaphorical, and the third meaning is real, and applying it to the real meaning is more appropriate than applying it to the metaphorical meaning; therefore, in the hadith, the third meaning of mutabay'i'an is intended. And when the third meaning is taken, i.e., after offer and before final acceptance, only khiyar al-qabul can be intended, not khiyar al-majlis. Thus it is established that by khiyar in the hadith, khiyar al-qabul is meant, and when khiyar al-qabul is intended, the aforementioned hadith cannot be a proof for Imam Shafi'i. And the second answer is from 'aw yuhtamalu'. Its summary is that even if khiyar al-qabul is not definitively intended in the hadith, the possibility of khiyar al-qabul also exists. That is, in 'al-bayyi'ani bi'l-khiyar', khiyar can mean khiyar al-qabul and it can mean khiyar al-majlis. But since taking it as khiyar al-majlis causes negation of another's right, it will be interpreted as khiyar al-qabul, not khiyar al-majlis. And by tafarruq, separation in statements is meant, i.e., khiyar al-qabul is established as long as the contracting parties do not separate verbally. And if both separate verbally, such that one said 'I sold' and the other said 'I bought', then after that no khiyar remains.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute where the Hanafi commentator refutes Imam Shafi'i's reliance on the hadith 'al-bayyi'ani bi'l-khiyar' to establish khiyar al-majlis. The Hanafi position is that the hadith refers to khiyar al-qabul (the option of acceptance) rather than khiyar al-majlis. Two arguments are given: First, the word mutabay'i'an (the two contracting parties) is taken in its real meaning of the present tense, which refers to the time between offer and acceptance, hence only khiyar al-qabul applies. Second, even if the word is ambiguous, it is interpreted as khiyar al-qabul to avoid harming the other party's right (as khiyar al-majlis would allow one party to revoke after acceptance, potentially harming the other). The passage also clarifies that 'tafarruq' (separation) here means verbal separation (i.e., exchange of words), not physical separation.

Key Terms
خیار قبول (khiyar al-qabul): The option of acceptance that exists between offer and final acceptance; it ends when both parties verbally agree.
خیار مجلس (khiyar al-majlis): The option to cancel the sale as long as the parties have not physically separated from the session.
متبابعان (mutabay'i'an): The two parties engaged in a sale; in the hadith, interpreted by Hanafis as referring to the state during the contract formation (present tense).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in this passage, what is the preferred interpretation of 'khiyar' in the hadith 'al-bayyi'ani bi'l-khiyar'?
A) Khiyar al-majlis (option of the session)
B) Khiyar al-qabul (option of acceptance)
C) Khiyar al-shart (stipulated option)
D) Khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects khiyar al-majlis by interpreting the hadith's 'khiyar' as khiyar al-qabul through linguistic and harm-prevention reasoning.

Pointed-to Consideration and Absolute Price in Sale
States rule for sale validity with pointed consideration vs. absolute price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for sale validity when consideration is pointed to or price is absolute, and identify which type of ignorance invalidates a sale.

Core Idea
Ignorance that leads to dispute invalidates a sale; ignorance that does not, does not.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains a key principle in Hanafi sales law: the distinction between jahala (ignorance) that invalidates and jahala that is tolerable. The ruling covers two scenarios: when the consideration is physically pointed to, and when the price is left absolute without specification. Understanding this distinction is essential for determining the validity of many everyday transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and note the two cases: (1) 'iwad mushar ilayhi (pointed-to consideration), (2) thaman mutlaq (absolute price).
2
Understand the ruling for each
For pointed-to: sale is valid even if quantity unknown. For absolute price: sale is invalid unless quantity and quality are known.
The reason given is the potential for dispute.
3
Recognize the underlying principle
The text says: 'Any ignorance that creates dispute prevents validity; any ignorance that does not, does not.' This is the central legal principle (qa'ida).
Jahalah mufdiyah ila al-munaza'ah is the impediment.
4
Note the exception for ribawi items
For ribawi items sold for their own genus (e.g., wheat for wheat), even pointing does not suffice if quantity is unknown, because of the possibility of riba.
Riba prohibition overrides the usual rule.
5
Apply the rule to a new case
Consider: a buyer has the option to choose one of two slaves. The sale is valid despite the unknown commodity, because the buyer's choice prevents dispute.
This illustrates that the test is always whether dispute is likely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قال والاعواض المشار اليها لا يحتاج الى معرفة مقدارها فى جواز البيع لان بالاشارة كفاية في التعريف وجهالة الوصف فيه لا تُفضى الى المنازعة والاثمان المطلقة لا تصح الا ان تكون معروفة القدر والصفة لان التسليم والتسلم واجب بالعقد وهذه الجهالة مفضية الى المنازعة فيمتنع التسليم والتسلم وكل جهالة هذه صفتها تمنع الجواز هذا هو الأصل

صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر شمن کی طرف اشارہ نہ کیا گیا ہو تو اس سے عقد اس وقت صحیح ہوگا جبکہ اس کی مقدار اور وصف دونوں معلوم ہوں اور اگر مقدار اور وصف دونوں معلوم نہ ہوں مثلا یہ کہا کہ میں نے اس چیز کو سونے کے عوض خرید لیا اور نہ اس کی مقدار بیان کی اور نہ اس کی صفت بیان کی تو یہ بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اور بیان مقدار کی صورت یہ ہے کہ کہے۔ میں نے اس چیز کو دس دینار کے عوض خریدا اور بیان صفت کی صورت یہ ہے کہ یوں کہے کہ وہ دینار بخاری ہیں یا سمرقندی ہیں جید ہیں یار دی ہیں بہر حال اگر شمن کی مقدار اور وصف معلوم نہ ہوں اور ثمن مشار الیہ بھی نہ ہو تو بیچ اس لئے نا جائز ہے کہ عقد بیع کی وجہ سے تعلیم اور تسلم یعنی دینا اور لینا واجب ہوتا ہے اور یہ جہالت یعنی مقدار اور وصف کی جہالت انجام کے اعتبار سے جھگڑا پیدا کرے گی۔ مثلاً مقدار مجہول ہونے کی صورت میں بائع زیادہ ثمن کا مطالبہ کرے گا۔ اور مشتری رڈی سپر د کر دے گا تو ایسی جہالت کی وجہ سے تسلیم اور تسلم مک ہوگا حالانکہ تسلیم او تسلم عقد بیع کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے پس جب تسلیم اور تسلم ناممکن ہوا تو بیع ہی درست نہ ہوگی ۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے ضابطہ کے طور پر فرمایا ہے کہ جو جہالت جھگڑا پیدا کرے وہ بیع جائز ہونے سے مانع ہے اور جو جہالت مفضی الی المنازعہ نہ ہو وہ جواز بیچ کے لئے مانع نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً کسی نے دو غلاموں میں سے ایک غلام فروخت کیا اور مشتری کو تعین کا اختیار دید یا تو مبیع مجہول ہونے کے باوجود بیع درست ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں جہالت اگر موجود ہے لیکن مشتری کو تعین کا اختیار دینے کی وجہ سے مفضی الی المنازعہ نہیں ہے۔
The ruling on pointed-to consideration and absolute price in sale. [Quduri] said: And the considerations that are pointed to do not require knowledge of their quantity for the validity of the sale, because pointing is sufficient for identification, and ignorance of the description in it does not lead to dispute. And absolute prices are not valid unless they are known in quantity and quality, because delivery and receipt are obligatory by the contract, and this ignorance leads to dispute, so delivery and receipt become impossible. And every ignorance of this nature prevents validity; this is the principle. Translation: Quduri said: Those considerations that have been pointed to do not need their quantity to be known for the sale to be valid, because for identification, pointing is sufficient, and ignorance of the description in it does not cause dispute. And as for absolute prices, the contract will not be valid unless their quantity and quality are known, because delivery and receipt are obligatory by the contract. And since this ignorance will cause dispute, giving and taking become impossible. And every ignorance of this nature prevents the validity of the sale; this is the principle. Explanation: The situation is that in a sale, whether the consideration is the price or the commodity, when it is pointed to, knowledge of its quantity is not required for the validity of the sale. For example, if he said, 'I bought this heap of wheat in exchange for these dirhams that are in my hand,' then this sale is valid, even though neither the quantity of the commodity (wheat) nor the quantity of dirhams is known. The proof is that pointing is sufficient for identification. And ignorance of the description, i.e., not knowing the quantity of the pointed-to object, is not something that creates dispute, whereas the impediment to validity is ignorance that creates dispute between the contracting parties. So when such ignorance is not present, the sale is valid. It is clear that if the considerations are of ribawi items, such as dirhams, dinars, wheat, and barley, and they are sold for their own genus and their quantity is unknown, this is not valid even if they are pointed to. For example, selling dirhams for dirhams or wheat for wheat with both quantities unknown is invalid even if both considerations are pointed to, because in this case there is a possibility of riba, and you know that just as riba is prohibited, so is the possibility of riba. In the text, the restriction to 'bay' is made to exclude salam, because according to Imam Abu Hanifa, in a salam sale, knowledge of the capital amount is a condition even if it is pointed to. The author of Quduri says: If the price is not pointed to, then the contract is valid only when its quantity and quality are both known. If both quantity and quality are unknown, e.g., he said 'I bought this thing in exchange for gold' without specifying quantity or quality, then this sale is not valid. The way to specify quantity is to say, 'I bought this thing for ten dinars,' and to specify quality is to say, 'These dinars are Bukhari or Samarqandi, fine or worn.' In any case, if the price's quantity and quality are unknown and the price is not pointed to, the sale is invalid because delivery and receipt are obligatory by the contract, and this ignorance (of quantity and quality) will lead to dispute. For example, when quantity is unknown, the seller will demand more price and the buyer will deliver poor quality, so due to this ignorance, delivery and receipt become difficult, while delivery and receipt are obligatory by the contract, so when delivery and receipt become impossible, the sale itself is not valid. The author of Hidayah stated as a rule: Any ignorance that creates dispute prevents the validity of the sale, and any ignorance that does not lead to dispute does not prevent validity. For example, if someone sold one of two slaves and gave the buyer the option to choose, then the sale is valid despite the commodity being unknown, because although ignorance exists here, it does not lead to dispute since the buyer has the authority to choose.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with explanation (expansion probe) from Ashraf al-Hidayah. It addresses two scenarios: when the consideration (whether price or commodity) is indicated by pointing (mushar ilayhi) and when the price is absolute (mutlaq) without specification. The ruling from Quduri is that pointing suffices for identification; ignorance of quantity in that case does not invalidate the sale because it does not lead to dispute. However, an absolute price (not pointed to) must be known in quantity and quality, otherwise the sale is invalid. The commentator explains the reasoning: delivery and receipt are obligatory, and ignorance that leads to dispute makes them impossible. An exception is made for ribawi items sold for their own genus: even pointing does not suffice because any ignorance of quantity creates the possibility of riba, which is prohibited. The rule is encapsulated: ignorance that leads to dispute prevents validity; ignorance that does not lead to dispute does not. An example is given of selling one of two slaves with the buyer given the right to choose; this sale is valid because despite ignorance, no dispute arises.

Key Terms
عوض مشار الیہ ('iwad mushar ilayhi): The consideration (price or commodity) that is physically pointed to, making its identification clear despite unknown quantity.
ثمن مطلق (thaman mutlaq): A price that is not specified by pointing or description, mentioned only in a general sense (e.g., 'gold' without details).
جہالت مفضی الی المنازعہ (jahalah mufdiyah ila al-munaza'ah): Ignorance that leads to dispute between contracting parties, considered a legal impediment to validity of the sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a sale with a pointed-to consideration (mushar ilayhi) considered invalid despite the pointing?
A) When the quantity is unknown.
B) When the consideration is part of ribawi items sold for their own genus.
C) When the quality is unknown.
D) When the buyer has the option to specify.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a sale depends on whether the ignorance in the contract leads to dispute—pointing suffices for identification unless the item is ribawi and sold for its own genus.

8 min
Validity of Sale with Deferred Price when Term is Known
States ruling with proof and condition for deferred price sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale with deferred price and identify the evidence from the Quran and Sunnah that supports its validity.

Core Idea
A sale with deferred payment is valid if the term is known; ignorance of the term leads to invalidity due to uncertainty.

In this passage from Quduri's matn and its commentary, we learn that selling for a deferred price is permissible in the Hanafi school, provided the deadline for payment is clearly specified. The ruling is supported by both the general Quranic permission of trade and the specific example of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Let's examine the proof and the condition that makes this contract valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sale with a deferred price (thaman mu'ajjal). The ruling: it is valid (sahih) if the term is known.
If term unknown, sale is fasid.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two proofs: Quran 2:275 (Wa ahalla Allah al-bay') and the hadith of the Prophet buying food from a Jew with deferred payment and pawning his armor.
The hadith is narrated by Bukhari.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic verse is general ('amm) in permitting trade, and the Hanafi principle is that a general command indicates validity for all types of trade unless excluded. The prophetic action (fi'l) provides a specific precedent.
This is an example of istidlal bi al-amm.
4
Understand the essential condition
The term must be known; otherwise, ignorance (jahalah) leads to dispute (niza') and the sale becomes fasid.
The commentary explains the reason: seller demands early, buyer delivers late.
5
Note the practical consequence
In practice, a sale with an unknown term is invalid, while a known term makes it valid.
This applies to modern installment sales.

قال ويجوز البيع بثمن حال ومؤجل اذا كان الاجل معلوما لاطلاق قوله تعالى و احل الله البيع وعنه عليه السلام انه اشترى من يهودى طعاما الى اجل ورهنه درعه ولابد ان يكون الاجل معلوما لان الجهالة فيه مانعة عن التسليم الواجب بالعقد فهذا يطالبه به فى قريب المدة وهذا يسلم في بعيدها

A sale with a deferred price is also valid whenever. [Quduri] said: And a sale with a spot price and a deferred price is valid when the term is known, due to the generality of Allah's saying: 'And Allah has permitted trade' (2:275), and from him (peace be upon him) that he bought food from a Jew for a deferred term and pawned his armor with him. And the term must be known, because ignorance of it prevents the delivery that is obligatory by the contract, for this one (seller) will demand it in a short time and that one (buyer) will deliver it in a distant time. Translation: Quduri said: A sale for a spot price and a deferred price is valid provided the term is known, because the saying of Allah Almighty 'And Allah has permitted trade' is general, and it is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he bought some food from a Jew on credit for a term and pawned his armor with him. And knowledge of the term is necessary, because ignorance of the term would prevent the delivery of the price that is obligatory due to the contract, for the seller will demand it in a short period and the buyer will deliver it in a distant period. Explanation: There are three types of commodities (a'yan): (1) currencies, i.e., dirhams and dinars; (2) animals and houses, etc.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Quduri's matn and its commentary. It states that a sale with a deferred price (thaman mu'ajjal) is valid if the term (ajal) is known. The proof is the general permission of trade in the Quran and the specific practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who bought food on credit from a Jew and pawned his armor. Knowledge of the term is essential because ignorance would lead to dispute over the payment time: the seller might demand payment sooner and the buyer might delay longer. The commentary then begins a classification of commodities (a'yan) into three types, but only two are listed (currencies and animals/houses) before the text is cut off. This classification likely continued to a third type (such as foodstuffs) on the following page.

Key Terms
ثمن مؤجل (thaman mu'ajjal): A price that is deferred to a future date, as opposed to spot payment.
أجل معلوم (ajal ma'lum): A known term or deadline for payment, specified clearly to avoid ignorance.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Deferred Sale (Bay' Mu'aijal) with Known Term is Permissible
Ruling on deferred payment sale with condition of known term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on deferred sale, identify the condition of known term, and apply the proofs from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
A deferred sale is valid only if the term is known — ignorance leads to dispute, which invalidates the sale.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from the Hanafi school on deferred payment sales (bay' mu'aijal). The passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies that deferred sales are permissible just like cash sales, provided the term of deferment is clearly specified. We will explore the textual proofs and the legal rationale for this condition, and see how ignorance of the term renders the sale invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Read the matn: the sale is valid with immediate or deferred price if the term is known. Note that if the term is unknown, the sale is fasid.
The condition (shart) is that the ajal must be ma'lum.
2
Locate the proofs (dalil)
The author cites two proofs: the Quranic verse 'Allah has permitted trade' (al-Baqarah 2:275) and the prophetic hadith of the Prophet buying food from a Jew on credit.
The Quranic proof is general ('amm); the Hadith demonstrates practical application.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves)
The general permission includes all types of sales, cash and deferred. The Hadith shows the Prophet himself engaged in a deferred sale, setting a precedent.
The Hanafi school holds that 'amm is qat'i until takhsis.
4
Analyze the condition: why must the term be known?
The text explains that ignorance of the term prevents the delivery of the price, leading to dispute. Any jahalah that causes dispute invalidates the contract.
This is based on the principle that uncertainty (gharar) in essential terms leads to fasād.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the term is known, the sale is sahih; if unknown, it is fasid. Other schools may have different views, but the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
This ruling affects many modern transactions like installments and credit sales.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدا جلد بهشتم
موزونات اور عددیات متقار بہ اگر وہ غیر نقدین کی بیع نقدین کے عوض ہوتو یہ بیع مبیع محض اور شمن محض پر مشتمل ہے یعنی اس میں نقدین کاشمن ہونا اور غیر نقدین کا مبیع ہونا متعین ہے اور اس کے علاوہ باقی دوسری صورتوں میں ہر ایک عوض شمن بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ اور بیچ بھی ہو ا سکتا سکتا ہے۔ البتہ لفظوں میں دخول باء اور عدم دخول باء کے ساتھ امتیاز ہو گا یعنی جس عوض پر بارہ داخل ہوگا وہ یمن کہلائے گا اور دوسرا عوض میچ کہلائے گا۔

He said: A sale is permissible with an immediate price or a deferred price if the term is known, due to the general meaning of the statement of Allah, 'And Allah has permitted trade,' and from him (peace be upon him) that he bought food from a Jew with a deferred term and pawned his armor. It is necessary that the term be known because ignorance of it prevents the delivery that is obligatory by the contract. So the seller demands it in a short period, while the buyer delivers it in a distant period. Translation: Quduri said: A sale with a cash price or a deferred price is permissible provided the term is known, because Allah's statement 'And Allah has permitted trade' is general, and it is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he bought some food from a Jew with a deferred term and pawned his armor with him. Knowing the term is necessary because ignorance of the term prevents the (delivery of) the price that is obligatory due to the sale contract. So the seller will demand it in a short period and the buyer will deliver it in a distant period. Explanation: There are three types of goods: (1) Currencies, i.e., dirhams and dinars; (2) Livestock and cloth, etc.; (3) Measured items like (goods sold by) measure. Weighted items and approximate countable items... if a sale of non-currency items in exchange for currency occurs, then this sale consists of a pure sold item and a pure price, i.e., here the currency is determined to be the price and the non-currency the sold item. In other cases, each countervalue can be the price and also the sold item. However, the distinction is made by the presence or absence of the letter 'ba' in the wording: the countervalue that has 'ba' attached to it is called the price, and the other countervalue is called the sold item. Now the issue is that a sale with cash and with deferred payment is permissible provided the deferred term is known. If the deferred term is unknown, the sale is invalid. The proof is that Allah Most High said, 'Allah has permitted trade' in general terms, i.e., trade is absolutely permissible, whether cash or deferred. Both are included under this verse. The second proof is the hadith of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that he bought some food from a Jew called Abu Hama on a deferred term and pawned his armor with him. In Sahih al-Bukhari, the wording is 'thirty sa' of barley.' i.e., he bought thirty sa' of barley. From the mentioned verse and narration, it is understood that just as a cash sale is permissible, similarly a deferred sale is also permissible. However, it is necessary that the deferred term be known, because ignorance of the term prevents the delivery of the price, while delivery of the price is obligatory due to the sale contract. It prevents delivery because the seller will demand the price in a short period, while the buyer will try to pay in a distant period. Thus a dispute arises. And since ignorance that leads to dispute prevents the validity of the sale, therefore the unknown term prevents the sale from being valid.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning deferred payment in sales. The matn from Quduri states that a sale is valid whether the price is paid immediately (hal) or deferred (mu'aijal), provided the term (ajal) is known. The commentator, al-Hidayah, provides two proofs: first, the Quranic verse 'Allah has permitted trade' (al-Baqarah 2:275), which is general and includes both cash and deferred sales. Second, the prophetic hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) purchased food from a Jew with a deferred term and pawned his armor as collateral. This shows the permissibility of deferred sales. The condition of knowing the term is essential because ignorance (jahalah) of the term prevents the obligatory delivery (taslim) of the price. If the term is unknown, the seller may demand payment immediately while the buyer expects a later date, leading to dispute (munaza'ah). Since any ignorance that leads to dispute prevents the validity of the sale, the term must be specified. The passage then briefly classifies types of goods (a'yan): currencies (nuqud), animals and cloth, and weighed/measured/counted items. It notes that in sales where currencies are exchanged for non-currencies, the currency is defined as the price (thaman) and the other as the sold item (mabi'). In other exchanges, each countervalue can be either depending on the wording (the letter 'ba' indicating the price). The conclusion reaffirms that deferred sales are permissible with a known term, and if the term is unknown, the sale is fasid (void). The Hanafi position here is that the sale is valid with a known term; the proof from Quran and sunnah establishes general permissibility, and the condition of known term is derived from the need to avoid dispute.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): Price or countervalue in a sale contract; can be cash or deferred.
مؤجل (mu'aijal): Deferred; a price payable at a future date.
أجل (ajal): Term or period of deferment; must be known to avoid dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A deferred sale (bay' mu'aijal) is valid in the Hanafi school provided the term (ajal) is known; ignorance of the term causes dispute and invalidates the sale.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Interpreting Absolute Price in Sales
Ruling on interpreting absolute thaman as prevalent currency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that an absolutely mentioned price (thaman mutlaq) is interpreted as the prevalent currency (ghalib nqd al-balad) and explain the underlying custom-based maxim.

Core Idea
When the price is not specified, custom determines the currency — the known has the force of a stipulation.

In sales, the price must be known for the contract to be valid. Often, the parties mention a quantity without specifying which currency they intend. How do we resolve this ambiguity? The Hanafi school, citing the maxim 'al-ma'ruf ka al-mashrut', refers to the most prevalent coin in that locality. This lesson unpacks the ruling from Quduri and the commentary from Al-Hidayah, showing how custom (urf) fills the gap and ensures the validity of the sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize when the price is 'absolutely mentioned' (thaman mutlaq): the quantity is stated but not the type or quality of currency.
2
Determine the default interpretation
According to the Hanafi school, the absolute price refers to the most prevalent (ghalib) currency of that city or market.
This is based on custom (urf) and the principle of seeking permissibility (taharri al-jawaz).
3
Apply the legal maxim
The maxim 'al-ma'ruf ka al-mashrut' (the known is like the stipulated) gives customary practice the same binding effect as an explicit condition.
4
Test with an example
If two coins of equal value exist, e.g., Bukhari and Samarqandi, but one is more common, the prevalent one becomes obligatory.
The ruling requires that the coins be equal in value; if they differ, the contract may be voidable (fasid) due to uncertainty.
5
Note the condition
This ruling applies when the currencies are of equal value. If they are of different values, the sale may be invalid because the price is not truly known.
The commentary explicitly assumes equal value; otherwise, the ambiguity is fatal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اطلق الثمن في البيع كان على غالب نقد البلد لانه المتعارف وفيه التحرى للجواز فيصرف اليه ترجمہ ... قدوری نے کہا کہ اور جس شخص نے بیچ میں شمن کو مطلق رکھا تو جوشن اس شہر میں سب سے زیادہ رائج ہو اس پر محمول ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہی متعارف ہے اور ایسا کرنے میں جواز بیع کا طلب کرنا بھی ہے اس لئے مطلق لفظ کو اسی کی طرف پھیرا جائے گا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شہر میں مختلف قسم کے سکے رائج ہوں اور مالیت میں سب برابر ہوں مثلاً کسی شہر میں بخاری اور سمر قندی دونوں سکوں کا رواج ہے اور مالیت دونوں کی برابر ہے تو ایسی صورت میں اگر شمن کو مطلق ذکر کیا یعنی مقدار کو ذکر کیا لیکن صفت ذکر نہیں کی۔ مثلاً یہ کہا کہ میں نے یہ چیز دس درہم کی خریدی ہے لیکن یہ نہیں کہا کہ وہ درہم بخاری ہوں گے یا سمر قندی ہوں گے ۔ تو اس کو غالب نقد بلد پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ جس سکہ کا رواج اور چلن زیادہ ہو متعارف وہی ہوتا ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ المعروف کا كالمشروط ، یعنی معروف اور متعارف کو وہی درجہ حاصل ہے جو مشروط کو حاصل ہوتا ہے پس کسی سکہ کی شرط کر دینے کی وجہ سے مشتری پر جس طرح مشروط امن واجب ہوتا ہے اس طرح عدم شرط کی صورت میں متعارف سکہ واجب ہوگا۔ اور متعارف وہ ہوگا جس کا چلن زیادہ ہو اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ شہر میں جس سکہ کا چلن زیادہ ہوشمن مطلق رکھنے کی صورت میں وہی واجب ہوگا۔
He said: And whoever makes the price absolute in a sale, it is interpreted according to the dominant currency of the city, because that is customary, and therein is seeking for permissibility, so it is referred to it. Translation: Quduri said: And a person who makes the price absolute in a sale, then it is construed as the most prevalent coin in that city, because that is customary, and in doing so there is also seeking for the permissibility of the sale, so the absolute wording is turned towards it. Explanation: The issue is: if in a city there are different types of coins in circulation and they are equal in value, for example, in a city both Bukhari and Samarqandi coins are common and their value is equal, then if the price is mentioned absolutely, i.e., the quantity is mentioned but the quality is not, for example, one says 'I bought this item for ten dirhams' but does not say whether the dirhams will be Bukhari or Samarqandi, then it will be interpreted according to the dominant currency of the city. Because the coin that has more circulation and use is the customary one, and the rule is 'the known is like the stipulated' (al-ma'ruf ka al-mashrut), i.e., what is known and customary has the same status as what is stipulated. So just as a stipulated coin becomes obligatory on the buyer due to the stipulation, similarly, in the absence of stipulation, the customary coin becomes obligatory. And the customary one is that which has more circulation. Therefore we said: the coin that has more circulation in the city, in the case of absolute mention of the price, that same one becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the interpretation of an absolutely mentioned price (thaman mutlaq) in a sale contract. The matn from Quduri states that when the price is mentioned without specifying the type of currency, it is taken to mean the prevalent (ghalib) currency of that city. The reason is that this is the customary usage (al-muta'arif), and applying it seeks the permissibility (taharri al-jawaz) of the sale. The commentary elaborates with an example: if in a city both Bukhari and Samarqandi coins are common and of equal value, and someone says 'I bought this for ten dirhams' without specifying, then it is interpreted as the more prevalent coin. This is based on the legal maxim 'al-ma'ruf ka al-mashrut' (the known is like the stipulated). Just as a stipulation makes a specific coin obligatory, so custom (urf) in the absence of stipulation makes the customary coin obligatory. The dominant coin is that which has wider circulation. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school and applies when the coins are equal in value; if they differ in value, the interpretation may differ. The passage thus provides a practical rule for resolving ambiguity in sales contracts.

Key Terms
ثمن مطلق (thaman mutlaq): Price mentioned without specifying the type or quality of currency.
متعارف (muta'arif): Customary; that which is commonly known and used in transactions.
المعروف كالمشروط (al-ma'ruf ka al-mashrut): Legal maxim: The known (custom) has the same effect as a stipulated condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person buys an item for ten dirhams without specifying which dirhams, and in the city both Bukhari and Samarqandi coins are equally valued but Bukhari is more common, what is the buyer obliged to pay according to the Hanafi school?
A) Any coin of his choice.
B) Bukhari coins.
C) Samarqandi coins.
D) Half from each.

Key Takeaway
An absolutely mentioned price in a sale is interpreted as the prevalent currency of the city, based on custom which has the force of a stipulation.

Determining the Currency for an Absolute Price in Sale
Discusses how to determine the currency when the price is left unspecified

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for an unspecified price in a sale to determine the obligatory currency and identify when the sale is valid or invalid.

Core Idea
Custom is like a condition: the prevalent currency becomes the price when unspecified.

A sale contract must have a known price to avoid dispute. When the price is left absolute—e.g., 'I sell this for ten dirhams' without specifying which dirham—Hanafi fiqh determines the currency by the custom of the place. This lesson unpacks the principle and its application to four possible scenarios of multiple circulating currencies, based on the text from al-Hidayah and al-Quduri.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Basic Ruling
Read the passage to extract the core ruling: an absolute price is interpreted according to the most prevalent currency of the town where the sale is conducted.
The town is the place of contract, not the parties' residence.
2
Understand the Legal Maxim
The ruling is grounded in the maxim 'al-ma'ruf ka al-mashrut' (the known/customary is like a stipulated condition). Custom serves as an implicit specification.
This maxim appears in the commentary.
3
Analyze the Four Scenarios
The passage logically divides into cases based on whether the circulating currencies differ in value (qima) or circulation (rawaj). Map each combination to its ruling.
The text explicitly lists three cases; the fourth (both equal) is derived from the third.
4
Apply the Ruling to a Given Case
Given a scenario with multiple currencies, determine the hukm: valid, invalid, or require specification. Use the matrix: circulation equal? value equal?
If circulation differs, the prevalent currency governs regardless of value.
5
Distinguish Ignorance vs. Dispute
The invalidating factor is 'jahalah' (ignorance) that leads to dispute. If value equality removes dispute, the sale is valid even without specification.
Equality of value eliminates the motive for conflict.

أويكون احدها اغلب واروج ..... الخ میں پہلی صورت کا بیان ہے یعنی اگر نفود مالیت اور رواج دونوں میں مختلف ہوں اس طور پر کہ مالیت میں بھی تفاوت ہے اور جلن میں بھی تفاوت ہے یعنی ایک سکہ کا چلن کم ہے اور ایک کا زائد ہے تو اس صورت میں بیچ درست ہوگی ۔ اور مشتری پر وہ سکہ واجب ہو گا جس کا چلن زیادہ ہے کیونکہ ایسا کرنے میں یعنی اغلب اور اروج پر محمول کرنے میں جو از بیچ کو طلب
On which currency does the absolute price apply?
He said: 'Whoever makes the price absolute in a sale, then it is interpreted according to the prevalent currency of the town, because it is customary and there is an effort to validate the sale, so it is referred to it.' Translation: al-Quduri said: A person who left the price absolute in a sale, then it will be interpreted according to the most prevalent coin in that city, because that is customary. And in doing so, there is also seeking the validity of the sale, so the absolute word is turned towards it.
Explanation: The ruling is that if there are different types of coins in a city, and they are equal in value, for example in a city both Bukhari and Samarqandi coins are in circulation and their value is equal, then if the price is mentioned absolutely, meaning the quantity is mentioned but the description is not mentioned, e.g., he said 'I bought this for ten dirhams' but did not say whether they are Bukhari or Samarqandi dirhams, then it will be interpreted according to the prevalent currency of the city. Because the coin with more circulation and usage is what is customary, and the principle is that the known (customary) is like the stipulated; i.e., what is known and customary has the same status as what is stipulated. So just as the stipulated coin becomes obligatory on the buyer due to the stipulation, similarly in the absence of stipulation, the customary coin becomes obligatory. And the customary is that which has more circulation. Therefore we said that the coin with more circulation in the city will be obligatory when the price is left absolute.
The second proof is that interpreting it according to the prevalent currency of the city seeks the validity of the sale. Therefore it is also turned towards the prevalent currency of the city. So by 'prevalent currency of the city' is meant the city where the sale took place, not the city of the contracting parties. Naqd is gold and silver that is not minted into jewellery etc.
'If the currencies are different, the sale is invalid unless he specifies one of them.' And this is when all are equal in circulation, because ignorance leads to dispute. Unless the ignorance is removed by specification, or one of them is more predominant and prevalent, then it is referred to it in an effort to validate. And this is when they differ in value. If they are equal in value, like the thanā'ī, thulāthī, and nasrī coins in Samarqand today, and the difference of 'adālī in Farghana, the sale is valid when the word 'dirham' is used. This is what they said, and it is referred to the quantity (specified) from whichever type, because there is no dispute and no difference in value.
Translation: Then if these currencies differ in value, the sale is invalid unless he specifies one of them. And this ruling is when all currencies are equal in circulation, because ignorance causes dispute. Unless the ignorance is removed either by specification or by one of them being more predominant and prevalent, then in that case it is referred to it so that the contract is valid. And all this is when all currencies differ in value. If these currencies are equal in value, like today in Samarqand the thanā'ī, thulāthī, and nasrī, and in Farghana the 'adālī are different, then the sale is valid when the word 'dirham' is used. This is what the later shaykhs said, and it is referred to the quantity specified from whichever type, because there is no dispute and no difference in value.
Explanation: This ruling has logically four cases: there will be difference in value and circulation, or no difference in either, or no difference in circulation but difference in value, or no difference in value but difference in circulation. The fourth case has already been explained in the previous ruling. The third case is explained in this text. He said: If all circulated currencies in the city differ in value and are equal in circulation, the sale is invalid, unless he specifies one of them. The proof is that in case of difference in value, ignorance of the coin creates dispute, because the seller will demand the coin of higher value and the buyer will try to give the coin of lower value. Such ignorance leads to dispute. Therefore in this case the sale becomes invalid. However, if the ignorance is removed by specifying one coin, the sale becomes valid.
'Or one of them is more predominant and prevalent...' etc. This explains the first case: if currencies differ in both value and circulation, such that there is difference in value and difference in circulation, i.e., one coin has less circulation and another has more, then in this case the sale is valid. And the coin with more circulation becomes obligatory on the buyer, because in doing so, i.e., interpreting according to the more predominant and prevalent, the validity of the sale is sought.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with reasoning. It addresses the situation when a price is mentioned in a sale but the specific type of currency (e.g., which dirham) is not specified. The Hanafi rule, based on the principle that custom is like a condition (al-ma'ruf ka al-mashrut), is that the price defaults to the prevalent currency of the place of contract. The author (al-Quduri) states this clearly. The commentary then expands into a discussion of four possible scenarios when multiple currencies exist: (1) both value and circulation differ; (2) both are equal; (3) circulation equal but value differs; (4) value equal but circulation differs (the fourth case was already handled). The text explains that if currencies differ in value but are equal in circulation, the sale is invalid unless the type is specified, because ignorance leads to dispute. If one currency is more prevalent, even if values differ, the sale is valid and the prevalent currency is due. If the values are equal (even if names differ), the sale is valid and any can be given. This entire discussion is based on avoiding dispute (gharar) and seeking validity of the contract. The authority weight is from al-Hidayah and its commentaries, reflecting the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Key Terms
مطلق ثمن (mutlaq al-thaman): The price mentioned without specifying the type of currency (e.g., just 'ten dirhams' without saying which dirham).
غالب نقد بلد (ghalib naqd al-balad): The most prevalent currency in the city where the sale takes place.
نقود مختلفہ (nuqūd mukhtalifah): Different types of coins circulating in a region, which may differ in value or circulation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a city where two coins are equal in circulation but different in value, what is the ruling if the price is left absolute?
A) Sale is valid, and the buyer may give either coin.
B) Sale is valid, and the buyer must give the more valuable coin.
C) Sale is invalid (fasid) unless the type is specified.
D) Sale is invalid and cannot be cured.

Key Takeaway
When the price is left absolute, it is interpreted by the prevalent currency of the place of contract, and if multiple currencies coexist, the validity depends on their circulation and value.

Sale with Unspecified Currency: Four Scenarios
Expansion of four scenarios of currency difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each of the four scenarios of currency difference in a sale and apply the conditions of specification and dominance.

Core Idea
A sale is valid when currency is specified or dominant; otherwise hidden ignorance invalidates it.

In a sale, the currency (naqd) used for payment may be unspecified. The Hanafi school divides such cases into four scenarios based on two factors: commonness (rawaj) and value (maliyyah). This lesson unpacks the rulings, showing that ignorance (jahalah) invalidates the sale unless removed by specification or dominance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two key factors
Recognize that the ruling depends on two attributes of the currency: its circulation (rawaj) and its monetary value (maliyyah). These create four combinations.
2
Scenario one: equal in both
When currencies are equal in circulation and value, ignorance does not lead to dispute, so the sale is valid even without specification.
3
Scenario two: equal circulation, different value
If circulation is equal but values differ, ignorance (which currency will be paid) causes potential dispute. The sale is invalid unless one currency is specified.
This is the core fasid case.
4
Scenario three: one dominant in circulation
Even if values differ, if one currency is clearly more common (aghlab wa araj), the sale is valid and payment is made in that dominant currency, because ignorance is removed by custom.
The principle of taharri (seeking validity) applies.
5
Scenario four: equal in value despite different names
When two currencies have the same value despite different names (like historical examples from Samarqand and Farghana), the sale is valid when the word 'dirham' is used, since no dispute arises.
Equality in value removes the harmful ignorance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان كانت النقود مختلفة فالبيع فاسد الا ان يبين احدها وهذا اذا كان الكل فى الرواج سواء لان الجهالة مفضية الى المنازعة الا ان ترتفع الجهالة بالبيان او يكون احدها اغلب واروج فحينئذ يصرف اليه تحريا للجواز وهذا اذا كانت مختلفة فى المالية فان كانت سواء فيها كالثنائى والثلاثى والنصرتى اليوم بسمرقند والاختلاف بين العدالى بفرغانة جاز البيع اذا اطلق اسم الدرهم كذا قالوا وينصرف الى ما قدر به من اى نوع كان لانه لا منازعة ولا اختلاف في المالية
If currencies are different, the sale is invalid unless one of them is specified. This is when all are equal in circulation, because ignorance leads to dispute. Unless ignorance is removed by specification, or one is more common and prevalent, then it is directed to it seeking validity. This is when they differ in value. If they are equal in value, like al-thina'i, al-thulathi, and al-nasriti today in Samarqand, and the difference among al-'adali in Farghana, the sale is valid when the word dirham is uttered. Thus they said, and it is directed to whatever amount measured from any type, because there is no dispute nor difference in value.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a sale when the currency (naqd) is not specified. The discussion is an expansion of the base text by Al-Quduri, commented upon by Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah and further explained in Ashraf al-Hidayah. The author outlines four scenarios based on two factors: circulation (rawaj) and value (maliyyah). First, if currencies are equal in both circulation and value, the sale is valid without specification. Second, if equal in circulation but different in value, the sale is invalid unless one currency is explicitly specified, because ignorance (jahalah) leads to dispute. Third, if one currency is dominant in circulation (even if value differs), the sale is valid and payment is made in that dominant currency, seeking validity (taharriyan lil-jawaz). Fourth, if they differ in both circulation and value, the same ruling as the third applies: the dominant currency is used. The text then gives examples from Samarqand and Farghana where coins are equal in value but different in name/circulation, ruling the sale valid. The principle is that jahalah is tolerated when it does not lead to dispute or when it is removed by specification or dominance.

Key Terms
نقد (naqd): Gold or silver coinage used as currency, not including jewelry.
رواج (rawaj): Circulation and commonness of a currency in a market.
مالية (maliyyah): Monetary value of a currency.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty about a necessary term of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a sale of unspecified currency valid even if the currencies have different names?
A) When the buyer chooses the currency at payment.
B) When the values are equal.
C) When the seller is a scholar.
D) When the price is low.

Key Takeaway
A sale is valid when payment currency is specified or dominant, or when currencies are equal in value; otherwise ignorance invalidates it.

Sale of Grains by Measure or Estimate with Same or Different Genus
Ruling on selling food grains by measure or estimate when exchanged for same or different genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling grains by estimate (mujazafah) when the genera differ and when they are the same, and apply the hadith proof to distinguish permissible from impermissible scenarios.

Core Idea
Selling grain by estimate is permissible if genera differ, but prohibited if same genus due to riba risk.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on selling food grains by measure or by estimate. The key distinction is whether the exchanged commodity is of the same genus or a different genus. Al-Hidayah cites a hadith to establish that when genera differ, estimate sales are valid provided spot delivery. However, same-genus estimate sales risk riba and are therefore invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Recognize that the text distinguishes between selling grain for a different genus and selling for the same genus.
The key factor is the genus of the counter-value.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
When sold for a different genus, the sale by estimate is permissible. When sold for the same genus, it is not permissible.
The ruling is clear: differing genera permit jahalah in quantity.
3
Extract the dalil (proof)
The hadith 'When the two types differ, sell as you wish, provided it is hand to hand' is the primary evidence.
The hadith is ahad but its indication is clear.
4
Explain the rationale
Same-genus estimate sales are prohibited due to the possibility of riba (usury) because equality in measure is required. Jahalah (ignorance of quantity) is not the problem as it is tolerated in other transactions.
The reasoning is based on preventing riba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجوز بيع الطعام والحبوب مكايلة ومجازفة وهذا اذا باعه بخلاف جنسه لقوله عليه السلام اذا اختلف النوعان فبيعوا كيف شئتم بعد ان يكون يدا بيد بخلاف ما اذا باعه بجنسه مجازفة لمافيه من احتمال الربوا ولان الجهالة غير مانعة من التسليم والتسلم فشابه جهالة القيمة
He said: The sale of food and grains by measure (makilah) and by estimate (mujazafah) is permissible. This is when he sells it for a different genus, due to his ﷺ saying: 'When the two types differ, sell as you wish, provided it is hand to hand.' Contrary to when he sells it for its own genus by estimate, because there is a possibility of riba, and because ignorance (jahalah) does not prevent delivery and receipt, so it resembles ignorance of price.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage expands the ruling from Al-Quduri's matn. It states that selling food (ta'am, usually wheat) and grains (hubub) by measure (mukayalah) or by estimate (mujazafah, i.e., without measuring) is permissible when sold for a different genus (e.g., wheat for barley). The proof is the hadith: 'When the two types differ, sell as you wish, as long as it is hand to hand' (i.e., spot transaction). However, if sold for the same genus by estimate, it is not permissible because it involves potential riba (since equality in measure is required in same genus exchanges). The author explains that jahalah (ignorance of exact quantity) in the exchanged counter-value does not prevent delivery and receipt, thus it is akin to ignorance of price (which is tolerated in non-ribawi transactions). This shows the Hanafi position: jahalah in the subject matter is not inherently invalidating if it does not lead to dispute and the transaction is spot.

Key Terms
مكايلة (mukayalah): Sale by measuring with a known measure (e.g., by volume or weight).
مجازفة (mujazafah): Sale by estimation without measuring or counting.
جنس (jins): Genus or type of commodity (e.g., wheat, barley).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is selling wheat by estimate (juzaf) for barley permissible?
A) Because barley is not a food
B) Because the types differ, so riba is not a concern
C) Because estimate is always permissible
D) Because ignorance of quantity is never a problem

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of estimate sale hinges on genus: different genus is valid; same genus is invalid due to riba risk.

Validity of Sale with Unspecified Currency Types When Equal in Value and Circulation
Stating the ruling when multiple currency types are equal in value and common usage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale when the buyer uses a general term like 'dirham' and multiple coin types of equal value are in circulation, and identify the condition that makes the sale valid.

Core Idea
When currencies are equal in value and circulation, a sale with an unspecified type is valid; the buyer may choose any type.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, the author clarifies a key condition for the validity of a sale when the buyer uses the general term 'dirham' without specifying which coin type. The ruling distinguishes between two situations: one where the currency types differ in value (sale invalid) and another where they are equal in both value and common usage (sale valid). Understanding this distinction prevents unnecessary invalidation of transactions based on ambiguity when no real dispute exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The buyer says 'I buy for 10 dirhams' without specifying which coin type, and multiple types are in circulation. The ruling depends on the relationship between these types.
2
Distinguish the two sub-cases
First case: currencies differ in value but are equally common → sale invalid. Second case: currencies equal in both value and circulation → sale valid. The passage focuses on the second case.
The cue 'فان كانت سواء فيها' signals the second case.
3
Identify the condition for validity
The text states that for sale to be valid, currencies must be equal in both value (مالیت) and circulation (رواج). If either differs, invalidity may arise.
4
Understand the rationale
The reason for validity is that when both value and usage are uniform, no dispute (جھگڑا) occurs between buyer and seller regarding the actual payment.
Dispute avoidance is a core principle in Hanafi muamalat.
5
Apply the examples
The Samarqand example: Nasri (full dirham), Sanai (2=1 dirham), Sulasi (3=1 dirham). The buyer may pay 10 Nasri, 20 Sanai, or 30 Sulasi. Similarly, modern Indian rupees: 10 rupees can be paid as one 10-rupee note, two 5-rupee notes, etc., provided no loss in change.
The condition 'provided no loss in change' ensures no gharar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ فساد بیع اس وقت ہے جب کہ نقود مالیت میں مختلف ہوں اور رواج میں برابر ہوں۔ فان كانت سَوَاء فيها الخ میں دوسری صورت کا بیان ہے۔ یعنی اگر نقود مالیت اور رواج دونوں پر برا بر ہوں تو مطلقا لفظ درہم بولنے سے بیع درست ہو جائے گی اور مشتری جس قسم میں سے چاہے درہم کی وہ مقدار ادا کرے جو بیان کی ہے یعنی دس یا میں جو مقدار بیان کی گئی تھی وہ ادا کرے اور جس قسم سے چاہے ادا کرے کیونکہ اس صورت میں نہ تو مالیت میں اختلاف ہے اور نہ کوئی جھگڑا پیدا ہوگا۔ نقود کے مالیت میں برابر ہونے کی مثال یہ ہے کہ جیسے آجکل سمرقند میں نصری ، ثنائی اور ثلاثی تین قسم کے سکے رائج ہیں اور مینوں کی مالیت برابر ہے بایں طور کہ نصرتی تو پورے ایک درہم کو کہتے ہیں اور یہ درہم والی سمر قند نصرۃ الدین کی طرف منسوب ہے اور ثنائی سے مراد وہ ہے جس کے دول کر ایک درہم ہوتا ہے اور ثلاثی سے مراد وہ ہے جس کے تین مل کر ایک درہم ہوتا ہے پس اگر سمر قند میں کوئی چیز دس درہم کی خریدی تو مشتری چاہے تو نصرتی دس درہم دیدے یا ثنائی جو دو ملا کر ایک درہم ہوتا ہے میں دیدے یا ثلاثی جو تین ملا کر ایک درہم ہوتا ہے۔ تمہیں دیدے جیسے آجکل ہندوستان میں اگر دس روپیہ کی کوئی چیز خریدی تو مشتری چاہے دس روپیہ دیدے یا میں اٹھنیاں دیدے یا چالیس چونیاں دیدے۔ سب درست ہے بشرطیکہ ریزگاری میں کچھ خسارہ نہ ہوتا ہو ۔ اسی طرح کا اختلاف فرغانہ میں عدالی سکہ میں ہے۔
The author of Hidayah says: This invalidity of sale occurs when the currencies differ in value but are equal in circulation. {فان كانت سواء فيها etc.} is the statement of the second case. That is, if the currencies are equal in both value and circulation, then absolutely by saying the word 'dirham' the sale becomes valid, and the buyer may pay the amount mentioned (i.e., ten or whatever amount was stated) from whichever type he wishes, and from whichever type he wishes he may pay, because in this case there is no difference in value nor will any dispute arise. An example of currencies being equal in value is like today in Samarqand there are three types of coins in circulation: Nasri, Sanai, and Sulasi, and their value is equal such that Nasri is called a full dirham and is attributed to Samarqand Nasrat al-Din, Sanai means two of them make one dirham, and Sulasi means three of them make one dirham. So if in Samarqand one buys something for ten dirhams, the buyer may give ten Nasri dirhams, or give Sanai (two make one dirham), or give Sulasi (three make one dirham). Similarly, in India today if one buys something for ten rupees, the buyer may give ten rupees, or give twenty half-rupees (athniya), or give forty quarter-rupees (chuniyan). All are valid provided there is no loss in the change. Similarly, a similar difference exists in the 'Adali coin in Farghana.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage explains a ruling from the Hidayah regarding the validity of a sale when the buyer uses the term 'dirham' without specifying which coin type, but multiple coin types are in circulation. The ruling distinguishes two scenarios: (1) if the coin types differ in value but are equal in circulation (common usage), the sale is invalid because it may lead to dispute; (2) if the coin types are equal in both value and circulation, the sale is valid and the buyer may choose any of the coin types to pay. The author provides examples from Samarqand (Nasri, Sanai, Sulasi coins) and from India (rupees, half-rupees, quarter-rupees) to illustrate. The key condition is that the currencies must be equal in value and in common usage, so no dispute arises. This ruling is based on custom (urf) and the principle of avoiding conflict.

Key Terms
نقود (nuqud): Currencies or coins used as medium of exchange
نصری (nasri): A full dirham coin from Samarqand attributed to Nasrat al-Din
ثنائی (sana'i): A coin such that two make one dirham
ثلاثی (sulasi): A coin such that three make one dirham

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When multiple currency types of equal value and common usage circulate, a sale with an unspecified type is valid; the buyer may pay with any type.

Selling Grain by Estimate: Valid with a Different Genus
Ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when selling grain by estimate (mujazafah) is valid according to the Hanafi school and explain the rationale using the hadith on ribawi items and the principle of riba suspicion.

Core Idea
Selling grain by estimate is valid only when exchanging for a different genus; same genus estimate triggers riba suspicion.

In this lesson, we examine a key Hanafi ruling on sales: selling food grains by estimate or by measure. The central distinction is whether the exchange involves the same genus or a different genus. The Prophet's hadith on ribawi items provides the proof, and the Hanafi school extends the logic to prohibit estimate when riba is suspected, while permitting it when such suspicion is absent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Distinguish between selling grain by estimate for a different genus (e.g., wheat for barley) and for the same genus (e.g., wheat for wheat). Note the different rulings.
2
Locate the hadith proof
Find the hadith 'When types differ, sell as you wish' in the passage. Understand that this is the primary dalil for permissibility when the genus differs.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Apply the riba suspicion principle
For same genus estimate, the sale is invalid due to 'suspicion of riba' (ihtimal al-riba). The Hanafi school treats such suspicion as equivalent to riba itself in prohibition.
This is a unique Hanafi extension to prevent any chance of riba.
4
Understand ignorance of quantity
The passage states that ignorance of quantity does not automatically invalidate a sale if it does not lead to dispute. Compare to ignorance of price, which is also tolerated.
This is the reason why estimate (juzaf) is not inherently corrupt.
5
Distinguish thaman and qimah
Note the useful distinction: thaman is the price agreed by the parties; qimah is market value determined by others. This helps contextualize the permissibility of ignorance of price.

Source Text

غلہ کی بیع جب خلاف جنس کے ساتھ ہو مکلیلہ و مجازفتہ دونوں طرح درست ہے

قال ويجوز بيع الطعام والحبوب مكايلة ومجازفة وهذا اذا باعه بخلاف جنسه لقوله عليه السلام اذا اختلف النوعان فبيعوا كيف شئتم بعد ان يكون يدا بيد بخلاف ما اذايا عه بجنسه مجازفة لمافيه من احتمال الربوا ولان الجهالة غير مانعة من التسليم والتسلم فشابه جهالة القيمة

ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور گندم اور اناج کو پیمانہ سے ناپ کر اور انداز سے بیچنا جائز ہے اور یہ اندازے سے بیچنے کا جائز ہونا اس وقت ہے جب کہ اس کو خلاف جنس کے عوض بیچا ہو ۔ کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جب دونوں قسم مختلف ہوں تو جس طرح چاہو فروخت کر و بعد اس کے کہ ہاتھوں ہاتھ ہو ۔ برخلاف اس کے جبکہ اس کو اس کی جنس کے عوض اندازے سے بیچا ہو ۔ کیونکہ اس میں ربوا کا احتمال ہے اور اس لئے کہ مقدار کا مجہول ہونا تسلیم اور تسلم سے مانع نہیں ہے۔ پس یہ قیمت مجہول ہونے کے مشابہ ہو گیا ہے۔

تشریح متن میں طعام سے مراد گندم اور اس کا آتا ہے۔ اور جنوب سے مراد دوسرے اناج ہیں۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ گندم اور دوسرے اناج کو پیمانہ سے ناپ کر بیچنا جائز ہے اور انکل اور اندازے سے بیچنا بھی جائز ہے۔ لیکن اندازے سے بیچنا اسی وقت جائز ہوگا جب کہ اس کو خلاف جنس کے عوض بیچا ہو۔ مثلاً گندم کو جو کے عوض فروخت کیا ہو اور اگر اس کی جنس کے عوض اندازے سے فروخت کرے تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں ربوا کا احتمال ہے اور احتمال ربوا اسی طرح ممنوع ہے جس طرح ربوا ممنوع ہے۔ اور خلاف جنس کے عوض اندازے سے بیچنے کے جواز کی دلیل حدیث ہے۔ پوری حدیث اس طرح ہے

الذهب بالذهب والفضة بالفضة والبر بالبر والشعير بالشعير والتمر بالتمر والملح بالملح مثلاً بمثل سواء بسواء يداً بيد فاذ اختلف هذه الاصناف فبيعو اكيف شئتم اذا كانت يدا بيد یعنی سونا ، سونے کے بدلے، چاندی، چاندی کے بدلے گندم گندم کے بدلے جو ، جو کے بدلے کھجور کھجور کے بدلے نمک، نمک کے عوض برابر سرابر ہاتھ درہاتھ بچو اور جب یہ انواع مختلف ہو جا ئیں تو جس طرح چاہے فروخت کرو جبکہ مجلس میں باہمی قبضہ ہو جائے۔

اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ اموال ربویہ میں اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں ہر طرح بیچنا جائز ہے۔ ناپ کر بھی اور اندازے سے بھی برابر سرا بر بھی اور کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ بھی۔ دوسری حدیث یہ ہے کہ اندازے سے بیچنے کی صورت میں عوضین کی مقدار کا مجہول ہونا تسلیم اور تسلم کے لئے مانع نہیں ہے ۔ اور مفسد بیچ وہی جہالت ہوتی ہے جو تسلیم اور تسلم کے لئے مانع ہو۔ پس جب یہ جہالت تسلیم اور تسلم کے لئے مانع نہیں ہے تو بیچ بھی فاسد نہ ہوگی۔ اور یہ قیمت مجہول ہونے کے مشابہ ہو گیا ۔ مثلاً کسی نے ایک درہم کے عوض کوئی سامان خریدا اور یہ معلوم نہیں کہ اس کی قیمت ایک درہم سے زائد ہے یا کم ہے یا برابر ہے۔ پس جس طرح قیمت کا مجہول ہونا مفضی الی المنازعہ نہ ہو نیکی وجہ سے مانع جواز نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں بھی عوضین کی مقدار کا مجہول ہونا مفضی الی المنازعہ نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مانع جواز نہ ہوگا۔ فوائد قیمت اور شمن کے درمیان فرق یہ ہے کہ ثمن اس کو کہتے ہیں جو عاقدین کے مابین مقرر کیا گیا ہے اور قیمت وہ ہے جس کو قیمت لگا نیوالے مقرر کرتے ہیں نہ کہ عاقدین۔
The sale of food and grains by measure and by estimate is permissible. This is when he sells it for something of a different genus, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'When the two types differ, then sell as you wish provided it is hand to hand.' Contrary to when he sells it for its own genus by estimate, because of the suspicion of riba, and because ignorance (of quantity) does not prevent delivery and receipt, so it resembles ignorance of the price.

Translation: Al-Quduri said: Selling wheat and grains by measure and by estimate is permissible, and this permissibility of selling by estimate is when he sells it for a different genus. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When the two types differ, then sell as you wish provided it is hand to hand.' Contrary to when he sells it for its own genus by estimate, because there is a suspicion of riba, and because the ignorance of quantity does not prevent delivery and receipt, so it resembles ignorance of the price.

Explanation: In the text, 'food' refers to wheat and its flour, and 'grains' refer to other grains. The issue is that selling wheat and other grains by measure is permissible, and selling by estimate is also permissible. But selling by estimate is only permissible when it is sold for a different genus. For example, selling wheat for barley. If he sells it for its own genus by estimate, it is not permissible, because there is a suspicion of riba, and suspicion of riba is prohibited just like riba itself. The proof for the permissibility of selling by estimate for a different genus is the hadith. The full hadith is: Gold for gold, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, like for like, equal for equal, hand to hand. But when these types differ, then sell as you wish provided it is hand to hand. That is: sell gold for silver, etc. This hadith establishes that in ribawi items, when the genus differs, all types of sales are permissible: by measure, by estimate, equal, or with surplus or deficit. Another hadith: In the case of selling by estimate, the ignorance of the quantity of the counter-values does not prevent delivery and receipt. The corruption of a sale is only due to ignorance that prevents delivery and receipt. So when this ignorance does not prevent delivery and receipt, the sale is not corrupt. It resembles the case of ignorance of the price. For example, someone buys an item for one dirham and does not know whether its price is more or less than a dirham or equal. Just as ignorance of the price does not prevent validity because it does not lead to dispute, similarly here, ignorance of the quantity of the counter-values does not prevent validity because it does not lead to dispute. Benefit: The difference between price (thaman) and value (qimah) is that thaman is what is agreed upon between the contracting parties, while qimah is what is determined by valuers, not by the contracting parties.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi ruling on selling food and grains by estimate (juzaf) or by measure (kayl). It is a ruling with proof from hadith. The key principle: when the exchange is with a different genus (e.g., wheat for barley), selling by estimate is permissible because the hadith says 'when the types differ, sell as you wish' as long as it is hand to hand. However, if it is the same genus (e.g., wheat for wheat), selling by estimate is not permissible because it creates a suspicion of riba (usury) due to potential inequality. The passage also discusses that ignorance of quantity does not invalidate the sale if it does not lead to dispute, comparing it to ignorance of price. The commentary distinguishes between thaman (price agreed by parties) and qimah (market value determined by others). This ruling is from the Hidayah and is authoritative (Zahir al-Riwayah).

Key Terms
مكايلة (mukayalah): Selling by measure (using a standard volume measure like a sa')
مجازفة (mujazafah): Selling by estimate or guess, without exact measurement
ربوا (riba): Usury or unlawful gain in trade, specifically prohibited by Shari'ah
ثمن (thaman): The price agreed upon by the contracting parties in a sale
قیمت (qimah): The market value or appraisal of an item, not necessarily the sale price

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi passage, why is selling grain by estimate for the same genus invalid?
A) Because the hadith forbids any sale by estimate.
B) Because it creates a suspicion of riba due to possible inequality.
C) Because ignorance of quantity always invalidates a sale.
D) Because the seller must always measure grain when exchanging for food.

Key Takeaway
Selling grain by estimate is valid only when the exchange involves a different genus; same genus estimate is invalid due to the strong Hanafi prohibition of anything leading to riba.
