Ruling on Selling with a Specific Vessel or Stone of Unknown Measure
Explaining the ruling with a qiyas-based proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling with a specific vessel or stone of unknown measure and explain why ignorance of quantity does not invalidate the sale when delivery is immediate.

Core Idea
Immediate delivery prevents dispute, so unknown quantity is tolerated in sale but not in salam.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn presents a key principle in Hanafi sales law: unknown quantity does not automatically invalidate a sale if it does not lead to dispute. The ruling hinges on the immediacy of delivery, contrasting with salam (forward sale) where deferred delivery makes ignorance problematic. The text also notes a disagreement among the Hanafi imams, with the majority view being the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
Al-Quduri states the ruling: it is permissible to sell with a specific vessel or stone even if its exact measure or weight is unknown.
2
Understand the rationale (illa)
The reason is that ignorance (jahalah) in this case does not lead to dispute (niza'), because delivery is immediate, making destruction of the vessel/stone before delivery rare.
This is a qiyas based on the absence of likely dispute.
3
Contrast with salam
In salam (forward sale), delivery is deferred, so destruction before delivery is not rare, and ignorance would lead to dispute. Hence, such a sale would be invalid in salam.
The contrast highlights the importance of delivery timing.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is not permissible even in sale, analogizing with salam. However, the majority (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit it.
The source confirms that the first opinion (permissible) is more correct (asahh) and more evident (azhar).
5
Apply the tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) is the majority view: the sale is permissible.
This is based on the principle of avoiding unnecessary restriction when dispute is unlikely.

Source Text

معين برتن معين پتھر کیسا تھ بیع کا حکم

قال ويجوز باناء بعينه لا يعرف مقداره وبوزن حجر بعينه لا يعرف مقداره لان الجهالة لا تفضى الى المنازعة لما انه يتعجل فيه التسليم فيندر هلاكه قبله بخلاف السلم لان التسليم فيه متاخر و الهلاك ليس بنا در قبله فيتحقق المنازعة وعن ابي حنيفة انه لا يجوزفى البيع ايضا والا ول اصح واظهر

ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور ایک معین برتن ( کی ناپ) کے ساتھ جس کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے اور ایک معین پتھر کے وزن کے ساتھ جس کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے (بیع کرنا ) جائز ہے کیونکہ مقدار کا مجہول ہونا جھگڑے تک نہیں پہنچتا کیونکہ اس سے بیع میں سپردگی فی الحال ہے تو اس معین برتن یا معین پتھر کا مبیع سپرد کرنے سے پہلے ہلاک ہو جانا امر نادر ہے۔ برخلاف بیع سلم کے کیونکہ بیع مسلم میں مبیع سپرد کرنا ایک مدت تک موخر ہو جاتا ہے۔ حالانکہ اس سے پہلے اس برتن یا پتھر کا تلف ہو جانا کوئی امر نادر نہیں ہے اس لئے جھگڑا پیدا ہوگا اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ بیع میں بھی نا جائز ہے لیکن قول اول اصبح اور اظہر ہے۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک معین برتن جس کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے اور معین پتھر جس کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے ان کے ساتھ بیچ کرنا جائز ہے مثلاً ایک شخص نے کہا کہ ایک روپیہ میں یہ بالٹی بھر کر دونگا یا ایک پتھر اٹھا کر کہا کہ ایک روپیہ میں اس کے وزن کے برابر گندم یہ یا اٹھا دونگا تو یہ بیع جائز ہے حالانکہ نہ یہ معلوم ہے کہ اس بالٹی میں کس قدر گندم آنا ہے اور نہ اس پتھر کا وزن معلوم ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں مبیع کی مقدار اگر چہ مجہول ہے لیکن مفضی الی المنازعہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ بیچ کے اندر میچ کو فوری طور پر سپر دکیا جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے
The ruling on selling with a specific vessel and a specific stone.

He (al-Quduri) said: It is permissible to sell with a specific vessel whose measure is not known, and with the weight of a specific stone whose measure is not known, because ignorance does not lead to dispute, since delivery is immediate in it, so its destruction before delivery is rare, unlike salam, because delivery in salam is deferred, and its destruction before that is not rare, so dispute arises. From Abu Hanifa it is narrated that it is not permissible even in sale, but the first opinion is more correct and more evident.

Translation: Al-Quduri said: Selling with a specific vessel (its measure) whose quantity is not known, and with the weight of a specific stone whose quantity is not known, is permissible because the ignorance of quantity does not lead to dispute, because in this sale delivery is immediate, so the destruction of that specific vessel or stone before delivery is a rare occurrence. Contrary to salam sale, because in salam delivery of the sold item is deferred for a period, and its destruction before that is not rare, so dispute arises. Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to have said it is not permissible even in sale, but the first opinion is more correct and more evident.

Explanation: The scenario is that selling with a specific vessel whose quantity is unknown and a specific stone whose weight is unknown is permissible. For example, a person says: 'For one rupee, I will fill this bucket (with something) and give it to you,' or lifting a stone says: 'For one rupee, I will give you wheat equal to the weight of this stone.' This sale is valid even though it is not known how much wheat the bucket holds nor the weight of the stone. The proof is that in both cases, the quantity of the sold item is unknown, but it does not lead to dispute, because in sale, delivery is made immediately, so...
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on the validity of a sale where the commodity is measured by a specific container (like a bucket) or weighed by a specific stone, both of unknown capacity or weight. The ruling from Al-Quduri and the majority is that such a sale is valid, because the ignorance (jahalah) of the quantity does not lead to dispute, since delivery is immediate and the destruction of the container/stone before delivery is rare. This is contrasted with salam (forward sale), where delivery is deferred and destruction before delivery is not rare, so ignorance would lead to dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa reportedly held that it is not permissible even in sale (analogous to salam), but the text states that the first opinion (permitting it) is more correct (asahh) and more evident (azhar). The commentary clarifies with examples: a person offering to fill a bucket for a fixed price, or to give grain equal to the weight of a stone. The rationale is that immediate delivery prevents dispute, making the sale valid despite the unknown exact quantity.

Key Terms
اناء (ina'): A specific container or vessel used for measuring the quantity of the sold item
حجر (hajar): A specific stone used as a weight reference for the sold item
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty about a vital aspect of the contract (here, quantity)
بیع سلم (bay' salam): A forward sale where payment is made in advance for deferred delivery of a commodity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Why is a sale valid when the quantity is measured by a specific bucket of unknown capacity, according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the bucket is known to the seller only.
B) Because immediate delivery makes destruction before delivery rare, so ignorance does not lead to dispute.
C) Because the buyer can reject the bucket after seeing it.
D) Because the hadith allows any type of sale.

Key Takeaway
A sale with a specific unknown-measure vessel or stone is valid because immediate delivery prevents dispute, contrasting with salam where deferred delivery makes such ignorance problematic.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Sale with a Specific Container or Stone of Unknown Measure
Ruling on sale using a specific container or stone of unknown measure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a sale with an unknown quantity measured by a specific container is valid in the Hanafi school and identify the intra-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
Ignorance (jahalah) invalidates a sale only if it leads to dispute; immediate delivery prevents dispute.

This passage examines a common transaction: selling 'this bucket full of wheat' without specifying the exact weight. The Hanafi school generally permits it, while Imam Abu Hanifa has a contrary narration. Understanding why this sale is valid reveals a key principle: jahalah is not always fatal; it only invalidates when it likely causes conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn states it is permissible (ja'iz) to sell using a specific vessel or stone of unknown measure.
The ruling is from the majority of Hanafi scholars.
2
Understand the reasoning
The author argues that ignorance does not lead to dispute (la tufdi ila al-munaza'ah) because delivery is immediate, making destruction of the container before delivery rare. Contrast this with salam (forward sale), where delivery is delayed and destruction is not rare, leading to dispute.
The key distinction is between immediate and deferred delivery.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa has a narration that such a sale is not permissible even in ordinary sale, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) allow it.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The first opinion (jawaz) is considered asahh (more correct) and azhar (more apparent), so it is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah prefers the majority view.

Source Text

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک معین برتن جس کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے اور معین پتھر جس کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے ان کے ساتھ بیچ کرنا جائز ہے مثلاً ایک شخص نے کہا کہ ایک روپیہ میں یہ بالٹی بھر کر دونگا یا ایک پتھر اٹھا کر کہا کہ ایک روپیہ میں اس کے وزن کے برابر گندم یہ یا اٹھا دونگا تو یہ بیع جائز ہے حالانکہ نہ یہ معلوم ہے کہ اس بالٹی میں کس قدر گندم آنا ہے اور نہ اس پتھر کا وزن معلوم ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں مبیع کی مقدار اگر چہ مجہول ہے لیکن مفضی الی المنازعہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ بیچ کے اندر میچ کو فوری طور پر سپر دکیا جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے مبیع سپرد کرنے سے پہلے اس برتن یا پتھر کا ہلاک ہونا نا در ہے اور جب اس کا ہلاک ہونا نا در ہے تو بائع اس متعینہ برتن سے ناپ کر یا اس متعینہ پتھر سے وزن کر کے مبیع مشتری کے حوالے کر دیگا۔ اور اس میں کوئی جھگڑا پیدا نہیں ہوگا۔ اور جب کوئی جھگڑا پیدا ہونے کا امکان نہیں تو بیچ بھی درست ہوگی کیونکہ بیع اس جہالت سے فاسد ہوتی ہے جو جہالت جھگڑے کا سبب واقع ہو۔ برخلاف بیع سلم کے کہ وہ معین برتن یا معین پتھر کے ساتھ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ بیع سلم کی صورت میں مبیع یعنی مسلم فیہ کی سپردگی ایک مدت کی تاخیر کے ساتھ عمل میں آتی ہے اور اس مدت میں اس معینہ برتن اور معینہ پتھر کا ہلاک ہونا نا در نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ ہلاک ہونا اغلب ہے تو اب عاقدین کے درمیان جھگڑا پیدا ہو گا اس طور پر کہ مسلم الیہ یعنی مشتری کہے گا کہ وہ برتن بڑا تھا اور رب اسلام یعنی بائع کہے گا کہ چھوٹا تھا اور جو جہالت مفضی الی المنازعہ ہو وہ مفسد ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے متعینہ برتن یا متعینہ پتھر کے ساتھ بیچ کرنا فاسد ہوگا حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ متعینہ برتن اور متعینہ پتھر جن کی مقدار معلوم نہ ہو ان کے ساتھ بیع کرنا بھی نا جائز ہے۔ جیسا کہ بیع سلم نا جائز ہے کیونکہ مکیلات اور موزونات میں بیج یا تو اندازے سے ہوتی ہے اور یا مقدار کو ذکر کر کے ہوتی ہے۔ پہلی صورت میں معقود علیہ کا مشار الیہ ہونا ضروری ہے اور دوسری صورت میں مقدار کا بیان کرنا ضروری ہے۔ اور یہاں دونوں چیزیں نہیں پائی گئیں اس لئے بیع جائز نہ ہوگی لیکن قول اول یعنی جواز کا قول اصبح بھی ہے اور اظہر بھی ہے۔
He said: And it is permissible (to sell) with a specific vessel whose measure is not known, and with a weight of a specific stone whose measure is not known, because ignorance does not lead to dispute, since delivery is immediate and its destruction before that is rare, contrary to salam because delivery is delayed and destruction is not rare before it, so dispute occurs. And from Abu Hanifa that it is not permissible in sale also, and the first is more correct and more apparent.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of a sale where the quantity is unknown but is measured by a specific container or stone. The relied-upon position (al-azhar) is that such a sale is valid, because the immediate delivery prevents dispute, unlike salam where delivery is delayed. The passage clarifies that ignorance (jahalah) only invalidates a sale if it leads to dispute. The example given is selling 'this bucket full of wheat' for a rupee. Although the exact quantity is unknown, the specific container/stone ensures delivery without conflict. Imam Abu Hanifa's transmitted view that it is also invalid is overridden by the stronger, more apparent opinion of the majority.

Key Terms
إناء (ina'): A specific vessel used to measure the sold item
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance about the quantity of the sold item
سلم (salam): A forward sale with deferred delivery of the sold item

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the container is accurately measured
B) Because immediate delivery makes destruction before delivery rare, preventing dispute
C) Because the buyer has the option to cancel

Key Takeaway
Jahalah only invalidates a sale if it leads to dispute; immediate delivery using a specific container or stone prevents such dispute, making the sale valid.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Sale of a Heap at Per-Unit Price: The One Qafiz Default
Intra-Hanafi dispute on a sale contract with unknown total quantity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the sale of a heap at a per-unit price and explain the qiyas used by each side.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa limits the sale to one qafiz to avoid jahalah; Sahibayn require it invalid unless ignorance removed.

When a seller offers a heap of grain at a fixed price per qafiz but does not state the total number of qafizes, the contract faces uncertainty (jahalah) in both subject matter and price. The Hanafi school splits on how to handle this: Abu Hanifa salvages one qafiz by analogy to an iqrar, while the Sahibayn hold the sale invalid unless the ignorance is removed. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and the core dispute
The contract: 'I sell you this heap, each qafiz for a dirham.' The total quantity unknown. The dispute: Abu Hanifa says valid for one qafiz; Sahibayn say invalid in both scenarios (with or without specifying total).
Both sides agree that jahalah is the issue.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof (qiyas to iqrar)
Abu Hanifa analogizes to someone who says 'I owe you a dirham for each dirham' – by consensus, only one dirham is owed. Here, the minimum known unit is one qafiz, so the sale is valid for that much.
This is a qiyas khafi because it's not an exact parallel but a hidden analogy.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof (qiyas to option sale)
The Sahibayn argue that ignorance removable by the parties (measuring or specifying) does not render the contract invalid, analogizing to the sale of one of two slaves with a buyer's option. In that case, ignorance of which slave is resolved by choice, so the sale is valid. Here, unresolved jahalah invalidates.
They hold that unless the ignorance is actually removed in the session, the contract fails.
4
Understand the consequence: buyer's option (khiyar al-tafarruq)
When the sale is valid for one qafiz (per Abu Hanifa), the buyer gets an option because the contract is split – he gets only part of what he intended. This is khiyar al-tafarruq.
Similarly, if the heap is measured or total specified after the contract, the buyer gains khiyar al-ru'yah (option of sight).
5
Apply the rule: when does ignorance disappear?
If the seller specifies the total qafizes or the heap is measured in the session, jahalah is removed for the whole, and the sale covers all qafizes. Then the buyer still has an option because now he knows the exact quantity.
This resolves the dispute practically: in practice, parties measure or specify to avoid the default.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن باع صبرة طعام كل قفيز بدرهم جاز البيع في قفيز واحد عند ابي حنيفة الا ان يسمى جملة قفزانها وقالا لايجوز في الوجهين له انه تعذر الصرف الى الكل لجهالة المبيع والثمن فيصرف الى الاقل وهو معلوم الا ان تزول الجهالة بتسمية جميع القفزان أو بالكيل فى المجلس وصار هذا كمالو اقرو قال لفلان على كل در هم فعلیه درهم واحد بالا جماع ولهما ان الجهالة بيد هما ازالتها ومثلها غير مانع كما اذا باع عبدا من عبدين على ان المشترى بالخيار ثم اذا جازفي قفيز واحد عند ابي حنيفة فللمشترى الخيار لتفرق الصفقة عليه و كذا اذاكيل فى المجلس اوسمى جملة قفزانها لانه علم بذالك الأن فله الخيار كما اذاراه ولم يكن راه وقت البيع
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور اگر کسی نے اناج کے ایک ڈھیر کو ایک قفیز بعوض ایک درہم کے حساب سے فروخت کیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک فقط ایک قفیز میں بیع جائز ہے مگر یہ کہ اس ڈھیری کے تمام قفیزوں کو بیان کر دے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ دونوں صورتوں میں جائز ہے امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس بیع کو تمام قفیزوں کی طرف پھر نا اس لئے متعذر ہے کہ مبیع اور رشن دونوں مجہول ہیں تو بیع کو سب سے کم کی جانب پھیرا جائے گا اور یہ معلوم بھی ہے مگر یہ کہ جہالت تمام قفیزوں کو بیان کر دینے یا مجلس میں ناپ دینے سے دور ہو جائے اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ کسی نے اقرار کیا کہ فلاں شخص کے مجھ پر کل درہم ہیں تو اس پر بالا جماع ایک درہم واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اور صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جہالت دور کرنا ان دونوں کے ہاتھ میں ہے۔ اور ایسی جہالت بیع جائز ہونے کو نہیں روکتی ہے۔ جیسے دو غلاموں میں سے ایک غلام اس شرط پر فروخت کیا کہ مشتری کو اختیار ہے۔ پھر جب امام صاحب کے نزدیک ایک قفیز میں بیع جائز ہوئی تو مشتری کو اختیار ہے۔ کیونکہ اس پر صفقہ متفرق ہو گیا اور اسی طرح اگر اسی مجلس میں وہ ڈھیر ناپ دیا گیا یا بائع نے اس کے تمام قفیز بیان کر دیئے کیونکہ اس
He said: And whoever sold a heap of food each qafiz for a dirham, the sale is valid for one qafiz according to Abu Hanifa, unless he specifies the total number of its qafizes. And they (the two) said it is not valid in both cases. His argument: it is impossible to refer the sale to the whole because of ignorance of the sold item and price, so it is referred to the minimum, which is known, unless ignorance is removed by specifying all qafizes or by measuring in the session. And this is like if he declared: 'For every dirham I owe so-and-so' then by consensus he owes one dirham. And their argument: ignorance can be removed by them, and such ignorance is not a barrier, as when he sells one of two slaves with the condition that the buyer has an option. Then when it is valid for one qafiz according to Abu Hanifa, the buyer has an option because the contract is divided for him. Similarly if he measured in the session or specified the total qafizes, because then he knows, so he has an option, as if he saw it and had not seen it at the time of sale.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of a heap of grain at a fixed price per qafiz without stating the total number of qafizes. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the sale is valid only for one qafiz, analogizing to a conditional acknowledgment (iqrar) where only one dirham is owed. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the ignorance is removable by measuring or specifying, so the sale is invalid altogether unless removed. However, when valid (per Abu Hanifa), the buyer has an option due to the contract being split (tafarruq al-safqah). The passage also notes that if the heap is measured in the session or total qafizes are specified, the buyer gains the option of sight (khiyar al-ru'yah) since he now knows the exact quantity.

Key Terms
صبرة (sibrah): A heap of grain or foodstuff sold in bulk
قفيز (qafiz): A unit of volume measurement for grains
صفقة (safqah): The contract or deal; 'tafarruq al-safqah' means the contract is split (i.e., buyer gets only part of what he intended)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if someone sells a heap of grain at 'each qafiz for a dirham' without specifying the total, how many qafizes are validly sold?
A) The entire heap
B) Only one qafiz
C) None; the sale is invalid
D) It depends on the buyer's choice

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's default rule: a sale with unknown total quantity is valid only for the minimum known unit, unless ignorance is removed.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

7 min
Selling with a Specific Container or Stone for Measurement
Ruling on using a designated mikyal or hajar for weighing in a sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using a designated mikyal or hajar in a sale, distinguish between immediate and salam sales, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on this issue.

Core Idea
A sale with a known container is valid if the container is durable; uncertainty leading to dispute invalidates.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from the Hanafi school: when a seller uses a specific container (mikyal) or stone (hajar) to measure the sold item, does the uncertainty about the exact quantity invalidate the sale? The passage draws a sharp distinction between spot sales and deferred salam sales, and even reveals a difference within the school itself. Understanding this ruling hones your ability to apply the principle that only jahalah mufdiyah ila al-munaza'ah (ignorance leading to dispute) voids a contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its General Ruling
The passage discusses a sale where the seller measures with a specific container (mikyal) or weighs with a specific stone (hajar). Determine the default ruling: is it permissible or impermissible?
The opening sentence states the container's destruction is rare, so the sale is valid.
2
Locate the Key Condition
The ruling hinges on the durability of the container. Identify what condition makes the sale valid and how the passage justifies it.
Condition: destruction before delivery is rare (naadir). If destruction is likely, dispute arises and the sale becomes invalid.
3
Analyze the Distinction Between Spot Sale and Salam
Contrast the ruling for an immediate sale with that for a defered salam sale. Explain why the same measurement method is invalid in salam.
In salam, delivery is delayed, so the container may perish; this creates jahalah leading to dispute.
4
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Identify the narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that opposes the first ruling. State his proof and reasoning.
Abu Hanifa's narration argues that in makilat/mawzunat, either estimation or precise quantity is required; here both are absent.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi Position
The author resolves the ikhtilaf by declaring the first opinion as asbah (sounder) and azhar (more apparent). Identify the operative ruling for fatwa.
The preferred position is permissibility when the container is durable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبیع سپرد کرنے سے پہلے اس برتن یا پتھر کا ہلاک ہونا نا در ہے اور جب اس کا ہلاک ہونا نا در ہے تو بائع اس متعینہ برتن سے ناپ کر یا اس متعینہ پتھر سے وزن کر کے مبیع مشتری کے حوالے کر دیگا۔ اور اس میں کوئی جھگڑا پیدا نہیں ہوگا۔ اور جب کوئی جھگڑا پیدا ہونے کا امکان نہیں تو بیچ بھی درست ہوگی کیونکہ بیع اس جہالت سے فاسد ہوتی ہے جو جہالت جھگڑے کا سبب واقع ہو۔ برخلاف بیع سلم کے کہ وہ معین برتن یا معین پتھر کے ساتھ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ بیع سلم کی صورت میں مبیع یعنی مسلم فیہ کی سپردگی ایک مدت کی تاخیر کے ساتھ عمل میں آتی ہے اور اس مدت میں اس معینہ برتن اور معینہ پتھر کا ہلاک ہونا نا در نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ ہلاک ہونا اغلب ہے تو اب عاقدین کے درمیان جھگڑا پیدا ہو گا اس طور پر کہ مسلم الیہ یعنی مشتری کہے گا کہ وہ برتن بڑا تھا اور رب اسلام یعنی بائع کہے گا کہ چھوٹا تھا اور جو جہالت مفضی الی المنازعہ ہو وہ مفسد ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے متعینہ برتن یا متعینہ پتھر کے ساتھ بیچ کرنا فاسد ہوگا حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ متعینہ برتن اور متعینہ پتھر جن کی مقدار معلوم نہ ہو ان کے ساتھ بیع کرنا بھی نا جائز ہے۔ جیسا کہ بیع سلم نا جائز ہے کیونکہ مکیلات اور موزونات میں بیج یا تو اندازے سے ہوتی ہے اور یا مقدار کو ذکر کر کے ہوتی ہے۔ پہلی صورت میں معقود علیہ کا مشار الیہ ہونا ضروری ہے اور دوسری صورت میں مقدار کا بیان کرنا ضروری ہے۔ اور یہاں دونوں چیزیں نہیں پائی گئیں اس لئے بیع جائز نہ ہوگی لیکن قول اول یعنی جواز کا قول اصبح بھی ہے اور اظہر بھی ہے۔
Before delivery of the sold item, the destruction of that container or stone is rare. When its destruction is rare, the seller will measure with that specific container or weigh with that specific stone and hand over the sold item to the buyer. And there will be no dispute in this. And when there is no possibility of dispute, the sale is valid, because the sale becomes invalid due to the ignorance that is a cause of dispute. Contrary to salam sale, because it is not permissible with a specific container or stone, because in salam the delivery of the sold item (muslam fihi) occurs after a delay, and during that period the destruction of that specific container or stone is not rare; rather destruction is preponderant. Then a dispute will arise between the parties: the muslam ilayh (buyer) will say the container was large and the rabb al-salam (seller) will say it was small. Ignorance that leads to dispute is invalidating. Therefore selling with a specific container or stone is invalid. There is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that selling with a specific container or stone whose quantity is unknown is also impermissible, just as salam is impermissible, because in makilat and mawzunat, sale is either by estimation or by mentioning the quantity. In the first case, pointing to the subject matter is necessary; in the second, stating the quantity is necessary. Here both are absent, so the sale is impermissible. But the first opinion (permissibility) is sounder and more apparent.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the validity of a sale using a specific container (mikyal) or stone (hajar) for measuring or weighing the sold item. The key condition is that the container must not be perishable before delivery; if it is rare to be destroyed, then the sale is valid because the uncertainty (jahalah) does not lead to dispute. The text contrasts this with a salam sale, where delivery is deferred and the container may perish, causing dispute. An intra-Hanafi difference is noted: a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa holds such a sale invalid altogether due to ignorance of the container's capacity. However, the author states that the first opinion (permissibility) is more sound (asbah) and more apparent (azhar). The reasoning revolves around the concept of jahalah mufdiyah ila al-munaza'ah—ignorance that leads to dispute invalidates a sale.

Key Terms
جھالت (jahālah): Uncertainty or ignorance about a crucial aspect of the subject matter or price in a contract.
بیع سلم (bayʿ salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance for goods to be delivered later.
مفسد (mufsid): An element that renders the contract invalid (fasid) in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a sale with a specific container (mikyal) valid in ordinary sale but invalid in salam?
A) Because in salam, the container is perishable
B) Because in salam, delivery is immediate
C) Because in salam, the container is not specified
D) Because in salam, the price is unknown

Key Takeaway
A sale using a specific measuring container is valid if the container is durable and delivery is immediate, because no jahalah leading to dispute exists.

Selling a Heap of Grain by the Qafiz Without Specifying Total Quantity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sale of grain heap

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute over the sale of a heap at a rate per qafiz without specifying total quantity and apply the rule regarding when ignorance of quantity invalidates or limits a sale.

Core Idea
Ignorance that can be easily removed does not invalidate a sale, but if removal is not done, only the minimum is enforceable.

In this passage, Imam al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a sale where the buyer says 'each qafiz for one dirham' without specifying the total number of qafiz in the heap. The key issue is whether the ignorance of the total quantity prevents the validity of the sale or merely limits it to one qafiz. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the principle of gharar (uncertainty) in sales and the distinction between removable and non-removable ignorance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and the source of ambiguity
The contract is a sale of a heap (subrah) of grain at a unit price per qafiz. The ambiguity lies in the unknown total number of qafiz, making both the subject matter (total quantity) and price (total price) uncertain.
This is a classic example of gharar in quantity.
2
State the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and his proof
Abu Hanifa rules that only one qafiz is validly sold, because the uncertainty cannot be resolved without specifying the total or measuring. He analogizes to an acknowledgment using 'every dirham' where only one dirham is due by consensus.
His proof relies on the principle that a word of generality ('kull') when attached to an unknown limit refers to the minimum.
3
State the position of the Sahibayn and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani rule that the entire heap is validly sold, because the ignorance can be easily removed by measuring in the session. They analogize to selling one of two slaves with a choice – the ignorance is temporary and does not prevent validity.
Their proof emphasizes that removable ignorance does not lead to dispute.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, only one qafiz passes, and the buyer may have an option due to split transaction. Under the Sahibayn, the entire heap is sold, and the buyer must accept the whole. The author notes that even if the sale is valid for one qafiz, the buyer has khiyar al-tafarruq because the transaction is split.
The question of whether the seller also gets an option is answered: the splitting affects the buyer's consent, not the seller's.

Source Text

الكل لجهالة المبيع والثمن فيصرف الى الاقل وهو معلوم الا ان تزول الجهالة بتسمية جميع القفزان أو بالكيل فى المجلس وصا رهذا كمالو اقرو قال لفلان على كل در هم فعلیه درهم واحد بالا جماع ولهما ان الجهالة بيد هما ازالتها ومثلها غير مانع كما اذا باع عبدا من عبدين على ان المشترى بالخيار ثم اذا جازفي قفيز واحد عند ابي حنيفة فللمشترى الخيار لتفرق الصفقة عليه و كذا اذاكيل فى المجلس اوسمى جملة قفزانها لانه کیا کہ فلاں شخص کے مجھ پر کل درہم ہیں تو اس پر بالا جماع ایک درہم واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اور صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جہالت دور کرنا ان دونوں کے ہاتھ میں ہے۔ اور ایسی جہالت بیع جائز ہونے کو نہیں روکتی ہے۔ جیسے مقدار بیان کردی یا کیل کر لیا گیا تو پورے ڈھیر کی بیع جائز ہو گی اور صاحبین نے فرمایا دونوں صورتوں میں پورے ڈھیر کی بیع جائز ہے۔ خواہ تمام قفیزوں کی مقدار بیان کی گئی ہو یا بیان نہ کی گئی ہو۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ چونکہ شمن اور مبیع دونوں مجہول ہیں اس لئے پورے ڈھیر میں بھیج کو جائز قرارد یا متعذر ہے۔ مبیع تو اس لئے مجہول ہے کہ ڈھیر کے تمام قطعیزوں کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے۔ اور جب صبیع مجہول ہے تو لازمی طور پر شمن بھی مجہول ہوگا۔ اور یہ جہالت مفضى الى المنازعہ اور جھگڑے کا سبب ہے۔ بایں طور کہ بائع اولا مشتری سے شمن پر قبضہ کا مطالبہ کرے گا اور چونکہ یمن غیر معلوم ہے اس لئے مشتری شمن اس وقت تک نہ دے گا جب تک اس کو یہ معلوم نہ ہو کہ مجھ پرشن کس قدر واجب ہے اور واجب شدہ چمن کی مقدار اس وقت معلوم ہوگی جبکہ مبیع کی مقدار معلوم ہو۔ پس اس طرح بائع اور مشتری دونوں نزاع اور جھگڑے کا شکار ہو کر رہ جائیں گے۔ بہر حال شمن اور مبیع مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے تمام قفیزوں میں بیع کو نافذ کرنا تو مستعد رہو گیا ہے اس لئے سب سے کم یعنی ایک قفیز جو معلوم بھی ہے اس کی طرف بیع کو پھیرا جائے گا کیونکہ لفظ کل جب ایسی چیز کی طرف مضاف ہو جس کی انتہا مقداد معلوم نہ ہو تو وہ سب سے کمتر کو شامل ہوتا ہے۔ پس مسئلہ مذکور میں جب کہ قفیز کہا حالانکہ یہ معلوم نہیں ہے کہ کل کتنے قیز ہیں تو فقط ایک قفیر کی بیع جائز ہوگی کیونکہ کمتر یہی ہے لیکن اگر جہالت مذکورہ تمنام قفیزوں کو بیان کر دینے یا مجلس کے اندکیل کر دینے سے دور ہو جائے تو پورے ڈھیر میں بیچ درست ہو جائے گی ۔ اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے کسی نے اقرار کیا کہ فلاں شخص کے مجھے پر کل درہم ہیں یعنی لفظ کل کے ساتھ مجھبول اقرار کیا تو بالا تفاق اس پر ایک درہم واجب ہوتا ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ مذکورہ میں مبیع یعنی تمام قضیزوں کی مقدار اگر چہ مجہول ہے لیکن اس جہالت کا ازالہ بائع اور مشتری دونوں کے ہاتھ میں ہے کیونکہ مبیع یعنی تمام قفیزوں کی مقدار جس طرح بائع کے ناپنے سے معلوم ہو سکتی ہے۔ اسی طرح مشتری کے کیل کرنے سے بھی معلوم ہو سکتی ہے پس جہالت مبیع کو دور کرنا بائع اور مشتری دونوں کی طرف سے ممکن ہے اور جب اس جہالت کو دور کرنا بائع اور مشتری دونوں کے ہاتھ میں ہے تو یہ جہالت مفضی الی المنازعہ نہ ہوگی اور جب یہ جہالت مفضی الی المنازعہ نہیں ہے تو جواز بیع کے لئے بھی مانع نہ ہوگی کیونکہ جواز بیع کے لئے وہی جہالت مانع ہوتی ہے جو جھگڑا پیدا کرے اور مفضی الی المنازعہ ہو اور اس جہالت بیع کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے کسی نے اپنے دوغلاموں میں سے ایک غلام کو اس شرط پر بیچا کہ مشتری کو ایک نام متعین کرنے کا اختیار ہے چاہے اس کو لے اور چاہے اس کو لے ۔ پس جب مشتری نے ایک غلام کو پسند کر لیا تو جہالت صبح دور ہوگئی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جب ایک قفیز میں بیع جائز ہوگی تو مشتری کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ ایک قفیر کو لے یا نہ لے۔ کیونکہ مشتری کے حق میں صفقہ متفرق ہو گیا ہے۔ بایں طور کہ پورے ڈھیر میں سے ایک فیز پر صفقہ باقی رہا اور جس پر صفقہ متفرق ہوتا ہے۔ چونکہ اس کی رضا مندی مختل ہو گئی ہے اس لئے اس کو لینے اور نہ لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ ایک سوال اور اس کا جواب رہا یہ سوال کہ صفقہ تو بائع کے حق میں بھی متفرق ہو گیا ہے لہذا اس کو بھی خیار حاصل ہو نا چاہیے تھا ۔ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ بلا شبہ بائع پر صلقہ متفرق ہو گیا ہے مگر یہ تفریق صفقہ اسی
The ruling on selling a heap of wheat, each qafiz for one dirham. He said: Whoever sells a heap of food, each qafiz for one dirham, the sale is valid for one qafiz according to Abu Hanifa, unless he specifies the total number of qafiz. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not valid in either case. His proof: It is impossible to refer the sale to the whole due to ignorance of the sold and the price, so it is referred to the least which is known, unless the ignorance is removed by specifying all the qafiz or by measuring in the session. And this is like if someone acknowledged: For so-and-so I owe every dirham, then one dirham is incumbent on him by consensus. Their proof: They have the ability to remove the ignorance, and such ignorance is not a preventing factor, just as if one sold one slave from two slaves with the condition that the buyer has the option. Then, when it is valid for one qafiz according to Abu Hanifa, the buyer has the option due to the splitting of the transaction. Similarly, if it was measured in the session or he specified the total number of qafiz, because now it is known, so he has the option, just as if he saw the sold item and had not seen it at the time of sale. Translation: Quduri said: And if someone sold a heap of food at one qafiz for one dirham, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the sale is valid only for one qafiz, unless he states all the qafiz. And the Sahibayn said: It is valid in both cases. Imam's proof: It is impossible to refer the sale to all the qafiz because the sold and the price are both unknown, so the sale is directed to the least, which is known, unless the ignorance is removed by stating all qafiz or by measuring in the session. And this is like someone acknowledging: For so-and-so, I owe every dirham, then by consensus one dirham is incumbent. Sahibayn's proof: They have the ability to remove the ignorance, and such ignorance is not a preventing factor, like selling one of two slaves with the condition that the buyer has the option. Then, when the sale is valid for one qafiz according to Imam, the buyer has the option due to the splitting of the transaction. Similarly, if the heap was measured in the session or the seller stated all qafiz, because now it is known, so the buyer has the option, just as when he saw the sold item though he had not seen it at the time of sale. Explanation of the case: A person sold a heap of saying: Each qafiz for one dirham. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the sale is valid only for one qafiz. However, if in that session he stated the quantity of all qafiz or measured it, then the sale of the whole heap is valid. The Sahibayn said: In both cases, the sale of the whole heap is valid, whether the quantity of all qafiz is stated or not. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: Since both the price and the sold are unknown, it is impossible to validate the sale for the whole heap. The sold is unknown because the quantity of all qafiz of the heap is unknown. When the sold is unknown, necessarily the price is also unknown. And this ignorance leads to dispute and is a cause of conflict. The seller will first demand the price from the buyer, and since the price is unknown, the buyer will not pay until he knows how much is due, and the amount of the due price will be known when the quantity of the sold is known. Thus, both seller and buyer will fall into dispute. In any case, due to the ignorance of the price and sold, executing the sale for all qafiz is impossible, so the sale is turned to the least, i.e., one qafiz, which is known, because the word 'kull' (every) when attached to something whose limit is unknown includes the minimum. So in this case, when he said 'every qafiz' while it is unknown how many qafiz there are, only the sale of one qafiz is valid because that is the minimum. But if the said ignorance is removed by stating all qafiz or measuring in the session, then the sale of the whole heap becomes valid. And this is like someone who acknowledged: For so-and-so, I owe 'every dirham', i.e., an acknowledgment using the word 'kull', then by consensus one dirham becomes due. Sahibayn's proof: In this case, although the quantity of the sold (all qafiz) is unknown, removing this ignorance is in the hands of both the seller and the buyer, because the quantity can be known either by the seller measuring or the buyer measuring. So removing ignorance is possible from both sides. When it is possible, this ignorance is not leading to dispute, so it does not prevent validity of the sale, because only ignorance that leads to dispute is a barrier. An example of such a sale is when someone sells one of his two slaves with the condition that the buyer has the option to choose which one—when the buyer chooses, the ignorance is removed. The author of Hidayah says: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when the sale is valid for one qafiz, the buyer has the option to take it or not, because the transaction is split with respect to him. That is, only one qafiz from the whole heap remains under the contract, and when the transaction is split, his consent is compromised, so he has the option to take or not. There remains a question: The transaction is also split with respect to the seller, so he should also have the option. The answer is that without doubt the transaction is split for the seller, but this splitting of the transaction...
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of a heap (surbah) of grain when the buyer says 'each qafiz for one dirham' without specifying the total number of qafiz. The passage presents the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that only one qafiz is validly sold, because the total quantity is unknown, leading to ignorance of both the subject matter and the price. This ignorance would lead to dispute, similar to an acknowledgment using 'every dirham' where only one dirham is due. However, if the total is specified or measured in the session, the sale becomes valid for the whole. The Sahibayn argue that since the ignorance can be easily removed (by measuring), it does not lead to dispute and thus the sale is valid for the whole heap. The author then discusses the khiyar (option) for the buyer: even when the sale is valid for one qafiz, the buyer has the option because the transaction is split (tafarruq al-safqah). A question arises about why the seller does not also get an option; the answer is that the splitting of the transaction affects only the buyer's consent, not the seller's. The text includes a comparison to an acknowledgment of debt and to a sale of one of two slaves with a choice.

Key Terms
صبرہ (ṣubrah): A heap of grain or similar commodity sold without specifying the total quantity.
قفیز (qafīz): A unit of dry measure, approximately 8-12 gallons depending on region, used for grains.
صفقہ متفرق (ṣafqah mutafarriqah): A transaction that is split, meaning only part of the intended contract is executed, giving the buyer an option.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn?
A) Whether the sale is valid or invalid
B) Whether the buyer has an option to rescind
C) The number of qafiz validly sold: one versus the entire heap
D) Whether the seller gets an option as well

Key Takeaway
In a sale of a heap at a rate per unit without specifying total, Abu Hanifa limits validity to one unit, while the Sahibayn validate the whole, due to differing views on removable ignorance.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Selling a Heap of Grain by Unit: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Dispute and reasoning on sale of unspecified grain heap per qafiz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the sale of an unspecified heap of grain per qafiz, explain their proofs using the concept of jahalah mufdiyah, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
When the total quantity is unknown, Abu Hanifa enforces only one unit; the Sahibayn enforce the whole if ignorance can be resolved.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of a sale where the price is per unit but the total quantity is unspecified. You will examine the reasoning of both sides and see how the concept of 'knowledge leading to dispute' determines validity. Finally, you will learn about the buyer's option (khiyar al-kashf) that applies when the quantity becomes known later.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two positions
Understand the basic sale: a heap of grain sold as 'each qafiz for a dirham' without stating total qafizes. Note that Imam Abu Hanifa says only one qafiz is valid; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the whole heap is valid.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that both the commodity (total qafizes unknown) and the price (derived from total) are unknown, creating jahalah mufdiyah ila al-niza' (ignorance leading to dispute). Since 'kull' when appended to an indefinite quantity refers to the minimum, only one qafiz is enforceable.
Analogy: iqrar (acknowledgment) with 'kull' similarly imposes only one dirham.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that the ignorance can be removed by either party measuring the heap, so it is not inevitably leading to dispute. They analogize to selling one of two slaves with buyer's choice: once chosen, ignorance is removed.
They consider the jahalah removable, hence not mufdiyah.
4
Compare the practical outcomes (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the seller can only claim payment for one qafiz; under Sahibayn, the seller can enforce the whole heap at the per-unit price. This affects the parties' leverage and the validity of the contract.
The passage does not definitively choose one position.
5
Understand the buyer's option (khiyar al-kashf)
When the total quantity becomes known later (e.g., seller measures), the buyer has an option to take the whole heap or cancel, because his expectation of quantity may differ. This is called khiyar al-kashf (option of discovery), similar to khiyar al-ru'yah.
This option exists even if the sale becomes valid for the whole according to Abu Hanifa after specification.

خیار حاصل ہو نا چاہیے تھا ۔ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ بلا شبہ بائع پر صلقہ متفرق ہو گیا ہے مگر یہ تفریق صفقہ اسی کی جانب سے آیا ہے بایں طور کہ بائع تمام قفیزوں کی مقدار بیان کرنے یا مجلس میں کیل کرنے سے رک گیا ہے پس جب تفریق صفتہ بائع کی جانب سے آیا تو بائع اس پر یقینا راضی ہوگا۔ اور جب بائع تفریق صفقہ پر راضی ہے تو تفریق صفقہ کی وجہ سے بائع کو اختیار دینے کے کیا معنی ہیں یعنی بائع کو کوئی اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس طرح اگر پوراڈ میر مجلس کے اندر کیل کر لیا گیا یا بائع نے ڈھیر کے تمام قطیر وں کی مقدار بیان کر دی تو بھی مشتری کو اختیار ہوگا مگر یہ اختیار سابقہ علت کی وجہ سے نہیں ہوگا بلکہ اس وجہ سے ہوگا کہ مشتری کے خیال میں اس ڈخیر کی مقدار کا ایک اندازہ تھا مثلاً اس کا خیال تھا اس ڈھیر میں ایک سو فقیر ہوں گے اور اتنی ہی تقریباً اس کی ضرورت تھی اور اتنے ہی روپیوں کا نظم تھا۔ اب جب بعد میں اس ڈھیر کونا پا یا بائع نے تمام قضیزوں کی مقدار بیان کی تو پتہ چلا کہ کل قفیز ایک سو سے زائد ہیں یا کم ہیں اگر زائد ہیں تو اس کی تین صورتیں ہیں ۔ (1 یہ کہ پورے کو پورے شمن کے عوض لے لے۔ (۲) یا ایک سو فیز کوشن کے عوض لے لے اور زائد کو مفت لے لے۔ اور یا زائد کو چھوڑ دے اور ایک سوکو لے لے۔ پہلی صورت تو اس لئے ممکن نہیں ہے کہ مشتری کے پاس ایک سو قفیز سے زائد کے لئے رقم نہیں ہے اور دوسری صورت یوں ممکن نہیں کہ بائع ایک سو فیز سے زائد اناج مفت کیوں دے گا اور تیسری صورت اس لئے ممکن نہیں کہ اس میں بائع پر تفریق صفقہ لازم آتا ہے اور اگر وہ ڈھیر ایک سو قفیز سے کم نکلا تو مشتری اپنی ضرورت کے مطابق ایک سو قفیز پورے کرنے کے لے زائدانان دوسری جگہ سے خریدے گا اب معلوم نہیں دوسری جگہ کا اناج اس کے موافق ہے یا نہیں ۔ بہر حال ان الجھنوں کی وجہ سے مشتری کو اختیار ہے کہ پورے ڈھیر کو کل قفیز بدر هم کے حساب سے لے لے یا پورے کو چھوڑ دے اس خیار کا نام خیار کشف ہے۔ کیونکہ کل مقدار جو عقد بیع کے وقت معلوم نہیں تھی وہ اب بائع کے بیان کر دینے یا کیل کر دینے سے معلوم ہوئی ہے اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے مشتری نے عقد بیع کے وقت مبیع کو نہیں دیکھا تھا بعد میں دیکھا تو مشتری کو لینے یا نہ لینے کا خیار حاصل ہے اسی طرح مسئلہ مذکورہ میں بھی مشتری کو لینے یا نہ لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔
Explanation of the case: A person sold a heap of grain saying 'each qafiz for a dirham'. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, only one qafiz is valid. If he specified the total or measured it in the session, the whole is valid. The Sahibayn said in both cases the sale of the whole is valid. Abu Hanifa's proof: because both price and commodity are unknown. The commodity is unknown because the total qafizes are unknown, so the price is necessarily unknown. This ignorance leads to dispute. The seller demands price, buyer doesn't know how much, so dispute. Therefore the sale is only valid for the least unit, one qafiz, because 'kull' when added to something indefinite means the least. If ignorance is removed by specification or measurement, the whole becomes valid. Sahibayn's proof: the ignorance can be removed by either party measuring, so it doesn't lead to dispute. Example: selling one of two slaves with buyer's choice; once chosen, ignorance is removed. The author of Hidayah says that when only one qafiz is valid ( Abu Hanifa), the buyer has the option to take or leave it because the contract is broken (tafarruq al-safqah) regarding the rest. A question: the seller also has a broken contract, so he should also have an option. Answer: the break is caused by the seller (he failed to specify), so he is content. Also, if the whole heap is measured in the session or specified, the buyer still has an option (khiyar al-kashf) because he had an expectation of the quantity. Three scenarios if more or less than expected. Due to these difficulties, the buyer has the option to take the whole at the rate or leave. This is khiyar al-kashf.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the sale of an unspecified quantity of grain per unit. Imam Abu Hanifa argues that since both the total commodity and the price are unknown, the sale can only be valid for the minimum unit (one qafiz). This is based on the principle that 'kull' when attached to an indefinite quantity refers to the least. The Sahibayn argue that the ignorance can be resolved by either party measuring, so the sale of the whole is valid. The author then explains that if only one qafiz is valid, the buyer has the option to take it or not because the contract is fragmented. A question arises: why doesn't the seller also have this option? The answer is that the fragmentation is due to the seller's omission, so he is deemed satisfied. Then, if the seller later specifies or measures, the buyer still has an option (khiyar al-kashf) because he had a mental estimate of the total quantity, and the actual quantity may differ, causing difficulty. This option mirrors the option of sight (khiyar al-ru'yah). The passage concludes that in such cases, the buyer may accept the whole or reject it.

Key Terms
جہالت مفضی الی المنازعہ (jahalah mufdiyah ila al-niza'): Ignorance that leads to dispute between parties, making a contract invalid.
خیار کشف (khiyar al-kashf): Option of discovery: buyer's right to cancel or confirm the sale when the true quantity becomes known after contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what happens if someone sells a heap of grain saying 'each qafiz for a dirham' without specifying the total number of qafizes?
A) The sale is valid for the entire heap.
B) The sale is valid only for one qafiz.
C) The sale is completely invalid.
D) The sale depends on the buyer's choice.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, sale of an unspecified quantity per unit is valid only for the minimum unit according to Abu Hanifa, while the Sahibayn uphold the whole if ignorance is removable, and the buyer retains khiyar al-kashf when the true quantity emerges.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Sale of Flock of Sheep by Unit: The Tafawut Distinction
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sale of unequal units, with distinction from grain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa invalidates the entire sale of a flock of sheep (each sheep for a dirham) while allowing the sale of one qafiz from a grain heap, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf with the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When items vary (tafawut), unspecified per-unit sales cause dispute; when uniform, jahalah is harmless.

In this passage, we learn a crucial distinction within Hanafi fiqh: the treatment of ignorance (jahalah) in sales depends on whether the units are uniform or vary in value. A flock of sheep and a piece of cloth by the cubit are examples of 'ma'dud mutafawit'—countable items with significant variation. This leads to an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn about the validity of such sales. Understanding this distinction is key to mastering the Hanafi rules of gharar and jahalah in transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested transaction
What is the exact sale scenario? (Flocks of sheep each for one dirham, no total stated; cloth by cubit each for one dirham, no total).
Also applies to any 'ma'dud mutafawit' (countable varied items).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa rules the entire sale fasid (invalid). His proof: significant variation (tafawut) among individuals leads to jahalah that necessarily causes dispute (mufdiyah ila al-niza').
Jahalah mufdiyah = ignorance that leads to dispute.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf & Muhammad) rule the sale valid for the whole. Their proof: jahalah can be removed by measuring or counting, similar to the grain heap case.
They apply qiyas to grain.
4
Trace the distinction from grain
Selling one qafiz from a grain heap is valid because grain is uniform (mutamathil); no tafawut, so jahalah does not cause dispute. In sheep/cloth, tafawut exists, so jahalah causes dispute.
Uniformity (adam al-tafawut) is the key differentiator.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: According to Abu Hanifa, the entire sale is nullified. According to Sahibayn, the sale is valid and parties can resolve the unknown total later.
The dispute has real-world impact on contract enforceability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن باع قطيع غنم كل شاة بدرهم فسد البيع في جميعها عند ابي حنيفة و كذالك من باع ثوبا مدارعة كل ذراع بدرهم ولم يسم جملة الذرعان وكذا كل معدود متفاوت وعندهما يجوزفى الكل لما قلنا وعنده ينصرف الى الواحد لما بينا غيران بيع شاة من قطيع وذارع من ثوب لا يجوز للتفاوت وبيع قفيز من صبرة يجوز لعدم التفاوت فلا تفضى الجهالة الى المنازعة فيه وتفضى اليها فى الأول فوضح الفرق ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے بکریوں کا ایک گلہ بعوض ایک درہم ایک بکری کے حساب سے فروخت کیا تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک تمام بکریوں کی بیع فاسد ہے اور اسی طرح اگر گزوں کی ناپ سے کوئی کپڑا بحساب ایک درہم فی گز کے فروخت کیا اور تمام گز بیان نہیں کئے اور یہی حکم
And whoever sold a flock of sheep, each sheep for a dirham, the sale of all of them is invalid according to Abu Hanifa. Similarly, whoever sold a piece of cloth by the cubit, each cubit for a dirham, and did not specify the total cubits, and likewise every counted item with variation. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the sale of all is valid for the reason we mentioned, and according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is restricted to one for the reason we explained. However, the sale of one sheep from the flock and one cubit from the cloth is not valid due to variation, while the sale of one qafiz from a heap is valid due to lack of variation. So ignorance does not lead to dispute in that case (grain) but leads to dispute in this case (sheep/cloth), thus the difference is clear. Translation: And the person who sold a flock of sheep in exchange for one dirham per sheep, according to Abu Hanifa the sale of all sheep is invalid. Similarly, if a cloth by cubit measurement is sold at one dirham per cubit and the total cubits are not specified, and the same ruling...
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute but focuses on the ruling for items with significant variation, such as sheep or cloth by the cubit. The same ikhtilaf applies: Abu Hanifa invalidates the entire sale for the whole flock or cloth because the ignorance (jahalah) is mufdiyah ila al-niza' (leads to dispute) due to the inequality of the units. The Sahibayn uphold the validity of the whole, as they did for grain, because the ignorance can be removed. However, there is a crucial distinction: selling a single sheep from a flock or a single cubit from a cloth is invalid even according to Abu Hanifa? Actually, the text says 'غير ان بيع شاة من قطيع وذارع من ثوب لا يجوز للتفاوت' meaning the sale of one sheep from the flock (without specification of which sheep) or one cubit from the cloth is not valid due to the variation. But note: in the grain heap case, selling one qafiz from the heap is valid because the grains are uniform. The difference is that grain is homogeneous, so there is no dispute; sheep and cloth are heterogeneous, so ignorance about which unit leads to dispute. Thus, the jahalah is mufdiyah in the latter but not in the former. This clarifies the distinction between the two rulings.

Key Terms
معدود متفاوت (ma'dud mutafawit): Countable items with significant variation in value or quality among individuals.
تفاوت (tafawut): Inequality or variation that renders a sale invalid if not specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa rule the sale of a flock of sheep (each sheep for a dirham without specifying total) as invalid, whereas he allows the sale of one qafiz from a grain heap?
A) Because sheep are living beings, while grain is not.
B) Because sheep vary in value (tafawut), causing dispute, while grain is uniform.
C) Because the sale of one qafiz from a heap is not allowed in any case.
D) Because the Sahibayn's opinion was followed for sheep.

Key Takeaway
The validity of per-unit sales without total depends on whether the units are uniform or varied; variation invalidates due to jahalah causing dispute (tafawut).
